{"uri": "2024-05-370367098", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-05-28", "time": "05:12:01", "dateTime": "2024-05-28T05:12:01Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-05-28T04:00:00Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.9529411792755127, "url": "https://omaha.com/life-entertainment/nation-world/travel/go-away-with-jessie-baylin-and-nathan-followill/article_8ab8d4e0-668c-52a0-a0b3-cf5f724a16fa.html", "title": "Go away with ... Jessie Baylin and Nathan Followill", "body": "Married musicians Jessie Baylin and Nathan Followill said Mexico City and anywhere in Thailand are on their travel bucket lists.\n\nJae-Ha Kim, Tribune Content Agency\n\nFor solo artist Jessie Baylin and Kings of Leon drummer Nathan Followill, this is an especially busy period for the married couple. In May, the Grammy Award-winning Kings of Leon released their latest album \"Can We Please Have Fun.\" And Baylin's May 31 re-release of her critically acclaimed 2018 album \"Strawberry Wind\" - \"Strawberry Wind (Deluxe Edition)\" - also includes new tracks. But with two young children, the musicians are mindful of making sure that one of them is at home with the kids. \"As of right now, I am not going to tour while the Kings are out,\" Baylin said. \"That could change, but I think right now the balance of having one of us home doing the routine with the kids is best.\" Baylin and Followill did this interview from their Nashville home. You may follow them on Instagram (@jezziebaylin and @thenathanfollowill) and X (@doctorfollowill). This interview has been edited for clarity and length.\n\nQ: Do you work on your material at home or on the road or both?\n\nJessie: All the original material on \"Strawberry Wind\" was written in Nashville over the course of a month - during the strawberry season. The new songs on the deluxe edition were also written while in town this past fall. I think I work best when I'm in the stillness of our home, though.\n\nQ: Jessie, can you share some of your memories of touring with Stevie Nicks?\n\nJessie: Opening for Stevie has been at the top of my mountain of dreams. It has been surreal. The crowds have been kind to me and have really taken in the music and I just love being in her vortex. She truly is one of the most generous of spirit people I have ever known. I love her very much.\n\nQ: When you're not touring, do you prefer to stay at home or take another trip?\n\nNathan: I'm a bit of a homebody. But I also live on a golf course, so I'm happy anywhere that I can get out and chase the little white ball around.\n\nQ: What are some travel memories you'd like to share?\n\nJessie: My parents are wanderlust people, so traveling was a part of my childhood. It wasn't often fancy, but we explored whenever we could. Growing up in New Jersey, the whole eastern coastline was our playground. We would spend time down at the Jersey Shore. Our favorite spot to spend a week every summer was Block Island, Rhode Island. My mom loves the Southwest and her life goal has always been to visit every national park. Right after Nathan and I met, I told him that I was leaving on a three-week family hiking trip through southern Utah. I was very difficult to get in touch with during that time. I think that is when he really fell for me! Nathan and I love exploring the Caribbean together. Our power move is tagging on a bonus holiday at the tail end of a big European tour before heading home.\n\nQ: Where have you traveled to for work that you went back to on a personal trip?\n\nNathan: We played the BottleRock Napa Valley [festival] and unfortunately had to fly in and out, but I always knew that I would go back and explore at some point. My wife and I were fortunate enough to make that happen with an amazing adults-only trip for her birthday.\n\nQ: Nathan, do you recall how you felt watching one of Jessie's shows?\n\nNathan: One of my favorite memories was running 10 blocks across Austin in high-heel boots after my set at SXSW so I could catch her set, and all I could think was, \"I hope I don't stink when I hug her after.\" She was a ball of expression and freedom that seemed like she didn't have a care in the world. I immediately gave her an\"I'm with the drummer\" T-shirt.\n\nQ: Are your children good travelers?\n\nJessie: Violet is a pro, Oliver is less so. [Laughs] He is a pandemic baby, so still a bit feral. But this past year, he's gotten the hang of it.\n\nNathan: As long as there is Wi-Fi, but, yes, they do enjoy it. We are blessed with very curious kids who are adaptive to Mommy and Daddy's lifestyle. Violet has more passport stamps than both my parents combined.\n\nQ: Which of you is the more efficient packer?\n\nJessie: One hundred percent me. I outfit plan and very rarely overpack.\n\nNathan: I'm a gypsy. My nickname is Piles, but I somehow always know where everything is.\n\nQ: What untapped destination should people know about?\n\nJessie: I'm very hesitant to share it because it is our paradise, but we love the Dominican Republic. It has some of the most beautiful beaches in the world and is rich with experiences. I love everything about it.\n\nNathan: Mine would be Copenhagen and Denmark, because every time you visit, you can have a totally different experience based on how basic or adventurous you want to be, especially with food.\n\nQ: What is your favorite vacation destination?\n\nJessie: This is difficult, but I have to say Italy. It is just such a beautiful country, and each region holds such magic and is different from the next.\n\nNathan: Dominican Republic. The people, the beaches, the golf and seeing how much joy it brings my kids.\n\nQ: What was a trip you took as a child that stands out?\n\nJessie: Santa Fe. I remember it vividly - the smell of pi\u00f1on wood, going to White Sands, the sound of the bats in the caverns, coyotes howling, eating fry bread from a stand in the middle of the desert. I totally fell for the Southwest forever on that trip. I was five.\n\nNathan: Our family reunion every year in the Tater Hills of Oklahoma where for one weekend a year, mosquito bites were currency.\n\nQ: What's the most important thing you've learned from your travels?\n\nJessie: Have your doctor call in a \"god forbid\" pack of medications.\n\nNathan: Always pack at least two outfits and your basics in your carry-on, and travel in something you could wear to dinner in a pinch.\n\nQ: If you could only pick one place to eat, would you prefer a food truck or fine dining?\n\nJessie: I love a food truck, but I don't love eating standing up or sitting on the curb. I prefer to enjoy a long thoughtful meal, though it doesn't have to necessarily be fancy. I'm going with fine dining.\n\nNathan: Give me a Frito pie and root beer from a truck and I'm one happy camper.\n\nQ: Where are your favorite weekend getaways?\n\nJessie: It would be a tie between Birmingham, Alabama, and Highlands, North Carolina.\n\nNathan: Charleston is 90 minutes door-to-door flight time and my dearest friends Luke and Lauren live there and are always down to show us where the locals like to eat.\n\nQ: What are your five favorite cities?\n\nJessie: Copenhagen, Zurich, London, Barcelona and Rio.\n\nNathan: Milan, Barcelona, Sydney, London and Singapore.\n\nQ: When you go away, what are some of your must-have items?\n\nJessie: Curling iron, journal and travel steamer.\n\nNathan: Golf clubs, peanut M&M's and a Tide pen.\n\nQ: What is your best and/or worst vacation memory?\n\nNathan: Best vacation memory is any summer I get to spend with my family on tour in fun cities. Worst vacation memory is getting sunburned so bad in Australia that my skin came off when I took off my socks.\n\n(Jae-Ha Kim is a New York Times bestselling author and travel writer. You can respond to this column by visiting her website at www.jaehakim.com. You may also follow \"Go Away With...\" on Twitter at @GoAwayWithJae where Jae-Ha Kim welcomes your questions and comments.)", "source": {"uri": "omaha.com", "dataType": "news", "title": "Omaha.com"}, {"uri": "8149139228", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-05-28", "time": "05:07:05", "dateTime": "2024-05-28T05:07:05Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-05-28T05:06:00Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.929411768913269, "url": "https://pantagraph.com/life-entertainment/nation-world/travel/go-away-with-jessie-baylin-and-nathan-followill/article_ee9f5e0c-c5bf-522e-8dff-ea8e2017389f.html", "title": "Go away with ... Jessie Baylin and Nathan Followill", "body": "Jae-Ha Kim, Tribune Content Agency\n\nFor solo artist Jessie Baylin and Kings of Leon drummer Nathan Followill, this is an especially busy period for the married couple. In May, the Grammy Award-winning Kings of Leon released their latest album \"Can We Please Have Fun.\" And Baylin's May 31 re-release of her critically acclaimed 2018 album \"Strawberry Wind\" - \"Strawberry Wind (Deluxe Edition)\" - also includes new tracks. But with two young children, the musicians are mindful of making sure that one of them is at home with the kids. \"As of right now, I am not going to tour while the Kings are out,\" Baylin said. \"That could change, but I think right now the balance of having one of us home doing the routine with the kids is best.\" Baylin and Followill did this interview from their Nashville home. You may follow them on Instagram (@jezziebaylin and @thenathanfollowill) and X (@doctorfollowill). This interview has been edited for clarity and length.\n\nQ: Do you work on your material at home or on the road or both?\n\nPeople are also reading... 'Gustnado' prompts sirens in Bloomington-Normal McLean County house rendered a total loss following weekend crash Bloomington educator retires after more than 40 years: 'Everyone has a job because of a teacher' Storms, blowing dust threaten Central Illinois Hudson man charged with armed robbery in McLean County Memorial Day parades, ceremonies planned in Central Illinois Normal police: 1 arrested after Thursday shooting on Shelbourne Carius: Remembering the site that housed many Bloomington restaurants, including Chevys Fresh-Mex Looking for something to do this weekend in Central Illinois? Here's the list. American Giants Museum bringing new statues to Atlanta upon first anniversary Miller Park Zoo to relocate female snow leopard, 'Shree' Bloomington man detained on attempted murder charge in May 7 shooting Funerals pending for May 25 Flick: When a job becomes a passion 1 injured in Shelbourne shooting; Normal police continue to investigate\n\nJessie: All the original material on \"Strawberry Wind\" was written in Nashville over the course of a month - during the strawberry season. The new songs on the deluxe edition were also written while in town this past fall. I think I work best when I'm in the stillness of our home, though.\n\nQ: Jessie, can you share some of your memories of touring with Stevie Nicks?\n\nJessie: Opening for Stevie has been at the top of my mountain of dreams. It has been surreal. The crowds have been kind to me and have really taken in the music and I just love being in her vortex. She truly is one of the most generous of spirit people I have ever known. I love her very much.\n\nQ: When you're not touring, do you prefer to stay at home or take another trip?\n\nNathan: I'm a bit of a homebody. But I also live on a golf course, so I'm happy anywhere that I can get out and chase the little white ball around.\n\nQ: What are some travel memories you'd like to share?\n\nJessie: My parents are wanderlust people, so traveling was a part of my childhood. It wasn't often fancy, but we explored whenever we could. Growing up in New Jersey, the whole eastern coastline was our playground. We would spend time down at the Jersey Shore. Our favorite spot to spend a week every summer was Block Island, Rhode Island. My mom loves the Southwest and her life goal has always been to visit every national park. Right after Nathan and I met, I told him that I was leaving on a three-week family hiking trip through southern Utah. I was very difficult to get in touch with during that time. I think that is when he really fell for me! Nathan and I love exploring the Caribbean together. Our power move is tagging on a bonus holiday at the tail end of a big European tour before heading home.\n\nQ: Where have you traveled to for work that you went back to on a personal trip?\n\nNathan: We played the BottleRock Napa Valley [festival] and unfortunately had to fly in and out, but I always knew that I would go back and explore at some point. My wife and I were fortunate enough to make that happen with an amazing adults-only trip for her birthday.\n\nQ: Nathan, do you recall how you felt watching one of Jessie's shows?\n\nNathan: One of my favorite memories was running 10 blocks across Austin in high-heel boots after my set at SXSW so I could catch her set, and all I could think was, \"I hope I don't stink when I hug her after.\" She was a ball of expression and freedom that seemed like she didn't have a care in the world. I immediately gave her an\"I'm with the drummer\" T-shirt.\n\nQ: Are your children good travelers?\n\nJessie: Violet is a pro, Oliver is less so. [Laughs] He is a pandemic baby, so still a bit feral. But this past year, he's gotten the hang of it.\n\nNathan: As long as there is Wi-Fi, but, yes, they do enjoy it. We are blessed with very curious kids who are adaptive to Mommy and Daddy's lifestyle. Violet has more passport stamps than both my parents combined.\n\nQ: Which of you is the more efficient packer?\n\nJessie: One hundred percent me. I outfit plan and very rarely overpack.\n\nNathan: I'm a gypsy. My nickname is Piles, but I somehow always know where everything is.\n\nQ: What untapped destination should people know about?\n\nJessie: I'm very hesitant to share it because it is our paradise, but we love the Dominican Republic. It has some of the most beautiful beaches in the world and is rich with experiences. I love everything about it.\n\nNathan: Mine would be Copenhagen and Denmark, because every time you visit, you can have a totally different experience based on how basic or adventurous you want to be, especially with food.\n\nQ: What is your favorite vacation destination?\n\nJessie: This is difficult, but I have to say Italy. It is just such a beautiful country, and each region holds such magic and is different from the next.\n\nNathan: Dominican Republic. The people, the beaches, the golf and seeing how much joy it brings my kids.\n\nQ: What was a trip you took as a child that stands out?\n\nJessie: Santa Fe. I remember it vividly - the smell of pi\u00f1on wood, going to White Sands, the sound of the bats in the caverns, coyotes howling, eating fry bread from a stand in the middle of the desert. I totally fell for the Southwest forever on that trip. I was five.\n\nNathan: Our family reunion every year in the Tater Hills of Oklahoma where for one weekend a year, mosquito bites were currency.\n\nQ: What's the most important thing you've learned from your travels?\n\nJessie: Have your doctor call in a \"god forbid\" pack of medications.\n\nNathan: Always pack at least two outfits and your basics in your carry-on, and travel in something you could wear to dinner in a pinch.\n\nQ: If you could only pick one place to eat, would you prefer a food truck or fine dining?\n\nJessie: I love a food truck, but I don't love eating standing up or sitting on the curb. I prefer to enjoy a long thoughtful meal, though it doesn't have to necessarily be fancy. I'm going with fine dining.\n\nNathan: Give me a Frito pie and root beer from a truck and I'm one happy camper.\n\nQ: Where are your favorite weekend getaways?\n\nJessie: It would be a tie between Birmingham, Alabama, and Highlands, North Carolina.\n\nNathan: Charleston is 90 minutes door-to-door flight time and my dearest friends Luke and Lauren live there and are always down to show us where the locals like to eat.\n\nQ: What are your five favorite cities?\n\nJessie: Copenhagen, Zurich, London, Barcelona and Rio.\n\nNathan: Milan, Barcelona, Sydney, London and Singapore.\n\nQ: When you go away, what are some of your must-have items?\n\nJessie: Curling iron, journal and travel steamer.\n\nNathan: Golf clubs, peanut M&M's and a Tide pen.\n\nQ: What is your best and/or worst vacation memory?\n\nNathan: Best vacation memory is any summer I get to spend with my family on tour in fun cities. Worst vacation memory is getting sunburned so bad in Australia that my skin came off when I took off my socks.\n\n(Jae-Ha Kim is a New York Times bestselling author and travel writer. You can respond to this column by visiting her website at www.jaehakim.com. You may also follow \"Go Away With...\" on Twitter at @GoAwayWithJae where Jae-Ha Kim welcomes your questions and comments.)\n\nLove 0 Funny 0 Wow 0 Sad 0 Angry 0\n\nTags Dcc Easytravel101 Wire Tns {"uri": "8149142058", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-05-28", "time": "05:08:42", "dateTime": "2024-05-28T05:08:42Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-05-28T05:08:15Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.929411768913269, "url": "https://greensboro.com/life-entertainment/nation-world/travel/go-away-with-jessie-baylin-and-nathan-followill/article_d171abae-6d83-511d-9889-7bc9a24a4446.html", "title": "Go away with ... Jessie Baylin and Nathan Followill", "body": "Jae-Ha Kim, Tribune Content Agency\n\nFor solo artist Jessie Baylin and Kings of Leon drummer Nathan Followill, this is an especially busy period for the married couple. In May, the Grammy Award-winning Kings of Leon released their latest album \"Can We Please Have Fun.\" And Baylin's May 31 re-release of her critically acclaimed 2018 album \"Strawberry Wind\" - \"Strawberry Wind (Deluxe Edition)\" - also includes new tracks. But with two young children, the musicians are mindful of making sure that one of them is at home with the kids. \"As of right now, I am not going to tour while the Kings are out,\" Baylin said. \"That could change, but I think right now the balance of having one of us home doing the routine with the kids is best.\" Baylin and Followill did this interview from their Nashville home. You may follow them on Instagram (@jezziebaylin and @thenathanfollowill) and X (@doctorfollowill). This interview has been edited for clarity and length.\n\nQ: Do you work on your material at home or on the road or both?\n\nJessie: All the original material on \"Strawberry Wind\" was written in Nashville over the course of a month - during the strawberry season. The new songs on the deluxe edition were also written while in town this past fall. I think I work best when I'm in the stillness of our home, though.\n\nQ: Jessie, can you share some of your memories of touring with Stevie Nicks?\n\nJessie: Opening for Stevie has been at the top of my mountain of dreams. It has been surreal. The crowds have been kind to me and have really taken in the music and I just love being in her vortex. She truly is one of the most generous of spirit people I have ever known. I love her very much.\n\nQ: When you're not touring, do you prefer to stay at home or take another trip?\n\nNathan: I'm a bit of a homebody. But I also live on a golf course, so I'm happy anywhere that I can get out and chase the little white ball around.\n\nQ: What are some travel memories you'd like to share?\n\nJessie: My parents are wanderlust people, so traveling was a part of my childhood. It wasn't often fancy, but we explored whenever we could. Growing up in New Jersey, the whole eastern coastline was our playground. We would spend time down at the Jersey Shore. Our favorite spot to spend a week every summer was Block Island, Rhode Island. My mom loves the Southwest and her life goal has always been to visit every national park. Right after Nathan and I met, I told him that I was leaving on a three-week family hiking trip through southern Utah. I was very difficult to get in touch with during that time. I think that is when he really fell for me! Nathan and I love exploring the Caribbean together. Our power move is tagging on a bonus holiday at the tail end of a big European tour before heading home.\n\nQ: Where have you traveled to for work that you went back to on a personal trip?\n\nNathan: We played the BottleRock Napa Valley [festival] and unfortunately had to fly in and out, but I always knew that I would go back and explore at some point. My wife and I were fortunate enough to make that happen with an amazing adults-only trip for her birthday.\n\nQ: Nathan, do you recall how you felt watching one of Jessie's shows?\n\nNathan: One of my favorite memories was running 10 blocks across Austin in high-heel boots after my set at SXSW so I could catch her set, and all I could think was, \"I hope I don't stink when I hug her after.\" She was a ball of expression and freedom that seemed like she didn't have a care in the world. I immediately gave her an\"I'm with the drummer\" T-shirt.\n\nQ: Are your children good travelers?\n\nJessie: Violet is a pro, Oliver is less so. [Laughs] He is a pandemic baby, so still a bit feral. But this past year, he's gotten the hang of it.\n\nNathan: As long as there is Wi-Fi, but, yes, they do enjoy it. We are blessed with very curious kids who are adaptive to Mommy and Daddy's lifestyle. Violet has more passport stamps than both my parents combined.\n\nQ: Which of you is the more efficient packer?\n\nJessie: One hundred percent me. I outfit plan and very rarely overpack.\n\nNathan: I'm a gypsy. My nickname is Piles, but I somehow always know where everything is.\n\nQ: What untapped destination should people know about?\n\nJessie: I'm very hesitant to share it because it is our paradise, but we love the Dominican Republic. It has some of the most beautiful beaches in the world and is rich with experiences. I love everything about it.\n\nNathan: Mine would be Copenhagen and Denmark, because every time you visit, you can have a totally different experience based on how basic or adventurous you want to be, especially with food.\n\nQ: What is your favorite vacation destination?\n\nJessie: This is difficult, but I have to say Italy. It is just such a beautiful country, and each region holds such magic and is different from the next.\n\nNathan: Dominican Republic. The people, the beaches, the golf and seeing how much joy it brings my kids.\n\nQ: What was a trip you took as a child that stands out?\n\nJessie: Santa Fe. I remember it vividly - the smell of pi\u00f1on wood, going to White Sands, the sound of the bats in the caverns, coyotes howling, eating fry bread from a stand in the middle of the desert. I totally fell for the Southwest forever on that trip. I was five.\n\nNathan: Our family reunion every year in the Tater Hills of Oklahoma where for one weekend a year, mosquito bites were currency.\n\nQ: What's the most important thing you've learned from your travels?\n\nJessie: Have your doctor call in a \"god forbid\" pack of medications.\n\nNathan: Always pack at least two outfits and your basics in your carry-on, and travel in something you could wear to dinner in a pinch.\n\nQ: If you could only pick one place to eat, would you prefer a food truck or fine dining?\n\nJessie: I love a food truck, but I don't love eating standing up or sitting on the curb. I prefer to enjoy a long thoughtful meal, though it doesn't have to necessarily be fancy. I'm going with fine dining.\n\nNathan: Give me a Frito pie and root beer from a truck and I'm one happy camper.\n\nQ: Where are your favorite weekend getaways?\n\nJessie: It would be a tie between Birmingham, Alabama, and Highlands, North Carolina.\n\nNathan: Charleston is 90 minutes door-to-door flight time and my dearest friends Luke and Lauren live there and are always down to show us where the locals like to eat.\n\nQ: What are your five favorite cities?\n\nJessie: Copenhagen, Zurich, London, Barcelona and Rio.\n\nNathan: Milan, Barcelona, Sydney, London and Singapore.\n\nQ: When you go away, what are some of your must-have items?\n\nJessie: Curling iron, journal and travel steamer.\n\nNathan: Golf clubs, peanut M&M's and a Tide pen.\n\nQ: What is your best and/or worst vacation memory?\n\nNathan: Best vacation memory is any summer I get to spend with my family on tour in fun cities. Worst vacation memory is getting sunburned so bad in Australia that my skin came off when I took off my socks.\n\n(Jae-Ha Kim is a New York Times bestselling author and travel writer. {"uri": "8149163131", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-05-28", "time": "05:27:36", "dateTime": "2024-05-28T05:27:36Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-05-28T05:26:38Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.929411768913269, "url": "https://theeagle.com/life-entertainment/nation-world/travel/go-away-with-jessie-baylin-and-nathan-followill/article_5d9fc26d-e991-512c-8a01-d6d770063b7d.html", "title": "Go away with ... Jessie Baylin and Nathan Followill", "body": "Jae-Ha Kim, Tribune Content Agency\n\nFor solo artist Jessie Baylin and Kings of Leon drummer Nathan Followill, this is an especially busy period for the married couple. In May, the Grammy Award-winning Kings of Leon released their latest album \"Can We Please Have Fun.\" And Baylin's May 31 re-release of her critically acclaimed 2018 album \"Strawberry Wind\" - \"Strawberry Wind (Deluxe Edition)\" - also includes new tracks. But with two young children, the musicians are mindful of making sure that one of them is at home with the kids. \"As of right now, I am not going to tour while the Kings are out,\" Baylin said. \"That could change, but I think right now the balance of having one of us home doing the routine with the kids is best.\" Baylin and Followill did this interview from their Nashville home. You may follow them on Instagram (@jezziebaylin and @thenathanfollowill) and X (@doctorfollowill). This interview has been edited for clarity and length.\n\nQ: Do you work on your material at home or on the road or both?\n\nPeople are also reading... Tornado Watch for much of Texas until 8 p.m. Wednesday Victims identified in Thursday's shooting in College Station St. Joseph hospital in Bryan downgraded to Level III trauma center Inside the transformation of Kyle Field's playing surface from gridiron to soccer pitch Texas A&M selected to host NCAA baseball regional at Blue Bell Park Three men named in Chi Alpha lawsuit arrested for indecency with a child Texas A&M baseball team tabbed No. 3 seed, gets Texas in regional What a game Centerville baseball team wins series over defending state champ Harleton Texas A&M baseball hopes to be competitive in SEC Tournament, without risking health Texas A&M associate professor allegedly terminated for entering student's home Large hail in Texas possible by Friday night Texas A&M looks to upset top-ranked Texas in NCAA softball super regionals Top-seeded Texas rallies from 5-1 deficit to force third game against A&M Part of William J. Bryan Parkway to be closed Tuesday-Friday next week\n\nJessie: All the original material on \"Strawberry Wind\" was written in Nashville over the course of a month - during the strawberry season. The new songs on the deluxe edition were also written while in town this past fall. I think I work best when I'm in the stillness of our home, though.\n\nQ: Jessie, can you share some of your memories of touring with Stevie Nicks?\n\nJessie: Opening for Stevie has been at the top of my mountain of dreams. It has been surreal. The crowds have been kind to me and have really taken in the music and I just love being in her vortex. She truly is one of the most generous of spirit people I have ever known. I love her very much.\n\nQ: When you're not touring, do you prefer to stay at home or take another trip?\n\nNathan: I'm a bit of a homebody. But I also live on a golf course, so I'm happy anywhere that I can get out and chase the little white ball around.\n\nQ: What are some travel memories you'd like to share?\n\nJessie: My parents are wanderlust people, so traveling was a part of my childhood. It wasn't often fancy, but we explored whenever we could. Growing up in New Jersey, the whole eastern coastline was our playground. We would spend time down at the Jersey Shore. Our favorite spot to spend a week every summer was Block Island, Rhode Island. My mom loves the Southwest and her life goal has always been to visit every national park. Right after Nathan and I met, I told him that I was leaving on a three-week family hiking trip through southern Utah. I was very difficult to get in touch with during that time. I think that is when he really fell for me! Nathan and I love exploring the Caribbean together. Our power move is tagging on a bonus holiday at the tail end of a big European tour before heading home.\n\nQ: Where have you traveled to for work that you went back to on a personal trip?\n\nNathan: We played the BottleRock Napa Valley [festival] and unfortunately had to fly in and out, but I always knew that I would go back and explore at some point. My wife and I were fortunate enough to make that happen with an amazing adults-only trip for her birthday.\n\nQ: Nathan, do you recall how you felt watching one of Jessie's shows?\n\nNathan: One of my favorite memories was running 10 blocks across Austin in high-heel boots after my set at SXSW so I could catch her set, and all I could think was, \"I hope I don't stink when I hug her after.\" She was a ball of expression and freedom that seemed like she didn't have a care in the world. I immediately gave her an\"I'm with the drummer\" T-shirt.\n\nQ: Are your children good travelers?\n\nJessie: Violet is a pro, Oliver is less so. [Laughs] He is a pandemic baby, so still a bit feral. But this past year, he's gotten the hang of it.\n\nNathan: As long as there is Wi-Fi, but, yes, they do enjoy it. We are blessed with very curious kids who are adaptive to Mommy and Daddy's lifestyle. Violet has more passport stamps than both my parents combined.\n\nQ: Which of you is the more efficient packer?\n\nJessie: One hundred percent me. I outfit plan and very rarely overpack.\n\nNathan: I'm a gypsy. My nickname is Piles, but I somehow always know where everything is.\n\nQ: What untapped destination should people know about?\n\nJessie: I'm very hesitant to share it because it is our paradise, but we love the Dominican Republic. It has some of the most beautiful beaches in the world and is rich with experiences. I love everything about it.\n\nNathan: Mine would be Copenhagen and Denmark, because every time you visit, you can have a totally different experience based on how basic or adventurous you want to be, especially with food.\n\nQ: What is your favorite vacation destination?\n\nJessie: This is difficult, but I have to say Italy. It is just such a beautiful country, and each region holds such magic and is different from the next.\n\nNathan: Dominican Republic. The people, the beaches, the golf and seeing how much joy it brings my kids.\n\nQ: What was a trip you took as a child that stands out?\n\nJessie: Santa Fe. I remember it vividly - the smell of pi\u00f1on wood, going to White Sands, the sound of the bats in the caverns, coyotes howling, eating fry bread from a stand in the middle of the desert. I totally fell for the Southwest forever on that trip. I was five.\n\nNathan: Our family reunion every year in the Tater Hills of Oklahoma where for one weekend a year, mosquito bites were currency.\n\nQ: What's the most important thing you've learned from your travels?\n\nJessie: Have your doctor call in a \"god forbid\" pack of medications.\n\nNathan: Always pack at least two outfits and your basics in your carry-on, and travel in something you could wear to dinner in a pinch.\n\nQ: If you could only pick one place to eat, would you prefer a food truck or fine dining?\n\nJessie: I love a food truck, but I don't love eating standing up or sitting on the curb. I prefer to enjoy a long thoughtful meal, though it doesn't have to necessarily be fancy. I'm going with fine dining.\n\nNathan: Give me a Frito pie and root beer from a truck and I'm one happy camper.\n\nQ: Where are your favorite weekend getaways?\n\nJessie: It would be a tie between Birmingham, Alabama, and Highlands, North Carolina.\n\nNathan: Charleston is 90 minutes door-to-door flight time and my dearest friends Luke and Lauren live there and are always down to show us where the locals like to eat.\n\nQ: What are your five favorite cities?\n\nJessie: Copenhagen, Zurich, London, Barcelona and Rio.\n\nNathan: Milan, Barcelona, Sydney, London and Singapore.\n\nQ: When you go away, what are some of your must-have items?\n\nJessie: Curling iron, journal and travel steamer.\n\nNathan: Golf clubs, peanut M&M's and a Tide pen.\n\nQ: What is your best and/or worst vacation memory?\n\nNathan: Best vacation memory is any summer I get to spend with my family on tour in fun cities. Worst vacation memory is getting sunburned so bad in Australia that my skin came off when I took off my socks.\n\n(Jae-Ha Kim is a New York Times bestselling author and travel writer. {"uri": "2024-05-370371045", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-05-28", "time": "05:17:21", "dateTime": "2024-05-28T05:17:21Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-05-28T04:00:00Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.929411768913269, "url": "https://qctimes.com/life-entertainment/nation-world/travel/go-away-with-jessie-baylin-and-nathan-followill/article_e90c8ece-27c3-531d-82eb-6e2a4ef14b4d.html", "title": "Go away with ... Jessie Baylin and Nathan Followill", "body": "Married musicians Jessie Baylin and Nathan Followill said Mexico City and anywhere in Thailand are on their travel bucket lists.\n\nJae-Ha Kim, Tribune Content Agency\n\nFor solo artist Jessie Baylin and Kings of Leon drummer Nathan Followill, this is an especially busy period for the married couple. In May, the Grammy Award-winning Kings of Leon released their latest album \"Can We Please Have Fun.\" And Baylin's May 31 re-release of her critically acclaimed 2018 album \"Strawberry Wind\" - \"Strawberry Wind (Deluxe Edition)\" - also includes new tracks. But with two young children, the musicians are mindful of making sure that one of them is at home with the kids. \"As of right now, I am not going to tour while the Kings are out,\" Baylin said. \"That could change, but I think right now the balance of having one of us home doing the routine with the kids is best.\" Baylin and Followill did this interview from their Nashville home. You may follow them on Instagram (@jezziebaylin and @thenathanfollowill) and X (@doctorfollowill). This interview has been edited for clarity and length.\n\nQ: Do you work on your material at home or on the road or both?\n\nPeople are also reading...\n\nQuad-Cities weather updates: Q-C under severe thunderstorm watch until 9 p.m. Quad-Cities business openings, closings: Disc Replay, Starbucks Hy-Vee responds to concerns over closing Iowa stores, offers measures to ease transition Meta named as company considering Davenport for data center; state board OKs incentives Will charges be brought in Davenport building collapse? Investigative report to prosecutor Davenport woman accused of double murder moved to Marshall County Jail 'We will find you': Moline police arrest man accused of post-prom double murder Orion School Board hears complaints of book being removed from curriculum Two arrested on animal neglect charges Spartans prevail against rival Bulldogs, qualify for 4A state tournament Pending Death Notices for the Quad-Cities, May 23, 2024 Weather blog: Tornado watch expires for Quad-Cities area Kathleen \"Kathy\" Joyce Billingsley Storm causes suspected tornado, damage in Rock Island County 'Worst decision they ever made;' Residents hit hard by Hy-Vee's plan to close Rockingham Road store\n\nJessie: All the original material on \"Strawberry Wind\" was written in Nashville over the course of a month - during the strawberry season. The new songs on the deluxe edition were also written while in town this past fall. I think I work best when I'm in the stillness of our home, though.\n\nQ: Jessie, can you share some of your memories of touring with Stevie Nicks?\n\nJessie: Opening for Stevie has been at the top of my mountain of dreams. It has been surreal. The crowds have been kind to me and have really taken in the music and I just love being in her vortex. She truly is one of the most generous of spirit people I have ever known. I love her very much.\n\nQ: When you're not touring, do you prefer to stay at home or take another trip?\n\nNathan: I'm a bit of a homebody. But I also live on a golf course, so I'm happy anywhere that I can get out and chase the little white ball around.\n\nQ: What are some travel memories you'd like to share?\n\nJessie: My parents are wanderlust people, so traveling was a part of my childhood. It wasn't often fancy, but we explored whenever we could. Growing up in New Jersey, the whole eastern coastline was our playground. We would spend time down at the Jersey Shore. Our favorite spot to spend a week every summer was Block Island, Rhode Island. My mom loves the Southwest and her life goal has always been to visit every national park. Right after Nathan and I met, I told him that I was leaving on a three-week family hiking trip through southern Utah. I was very difficult to get in touch with during that time. I think that is when he really fell for me! Nathan and I love exploring the Caribbean together. Our power move is tagging on a bonus holiday at the tail end of a big European tour before heading home.\n\nQ: Where have you traveled to for work that you went back to on a personal trip?\n\nNathan: We played the BottleRock Napa Valley [festival] and unfortunately had to fly in and out, but I always knew that I would go back and explore at some point. My wife and I were fortunate enough to make that happen with an amazing adults-only trip for her birthday.\n\nQ: Nathan, do you recall how you felt watching one of Jessie's shows?\n\nNathan: One of my favorite memories was running 10 blocks across Austin in high-heel boots after my set at SXSW so I could catch her set, and all I could think was, \"I hope I don't stink when I hug her after.\" She was a ball of expression and freedom that seemed like she didn't have a care in the world. I immediately gave her an\"I'm with the drummer\" T-shirt.\n\nQ: Are your children good travelers?\n\nJessie: Violet is a pro, Oliver is less so. [Laughs] He is a pandemic baby, so still a bit feral. But this past year, he's gotten the hang of it.\n\nNathan: As long as there is Wi-Fi, but, yes, they do enjoy it. We are blessed with very curious kids who are adaptive to Mommy and Daddy's lifestyle. Violet has more passport stamps than both my parents combined.\n\nQ: Which of you is the more efficient packer?\n\nJessie: One hundred percent me. I outfit plan and very rarely overpack.\n\nNathan: I'm a gypsy. My nickname is Piles, but I somehow always know where everything is.\n\nQ: What untapped destination should people know about?\n\nJessie: I'm very hesitant to share it because it is our paradise, but we love the Dominican Republic. It has some of the most beautiful beaches in the world and is rich with experiences. I love everything about it.\n\nNathan: Mine would be Copenhagen and Denmark, because every time you visit, you can have a totally different experience based on how basic or adventurous you want to be, especially with food.\n\nQ: What is your favorite vacation destination?\n\nJessie: This is difficult, but I have to say Italy. It is just such a beautiful country, and each region holds such magic and is different from the next.\n\nNathan: Dominican Republic. The people, the beaches, the golf and seeing how much joy it brings my kids.\n\nQ: What was a trip you took as a child that stands out?\n\nJessie: Santa Fe. I remember it vividly - the smell of pi\u00f1on wood, going to White Sands, the sound of the bats in the caverns, coyotes howling, eating fry bread from a stand in the middle of the desert. I totally fell for the Southwest forever on that trip. I was five.\n\nNathan: Our family reunion every year in the Tater Hills of Oklahoma where for one weekend a year, mosquito bites were currency.\n\nQ: What's the most important thing you've learned from your travels?\n\nJessie: Have your doctor call in a \"god forbid\" pack of medications.\n\nNathan: Always pack at least two outfits and your basics in your carry-on, and travel in something you could wear to dinner in a pinch.\n\nQ: If you could only pick one place to eat, would you prefer a food truck or fine dining?\n\nJessie: I love a food truck, but I don't love eating standing up or sitting on the curb. I prefer to enjoy a long thoughtful meal, though it doesn't have to necessarily be fancy. I'm going with fine dining.\n\nNathan: Give me a Frito pie and root beer from a truck and I'm one happy camper.\n\nQ: Where are your favorite weekend getaways?\n\nJessie: It would be a tie between Birmingham, Alabama, and Highlands, North Carolina.\n\nNathan: Charleston is 90 minutes door-to-door flight time and my dearest friends Luke and Lauren live there and are always down to show us where the locals like to eat.\n\nQ: What are your five favorite cities?\n\nJessie: Copenhagen, Zurich, London, Barcelona and Rio.\n\nNathan: Milan, Barcelona, Sydney, London and Singapore.\n\nQ: When you go away, what are some of your must-have items?\n\nJessie: Curling iron, journal and travel steamer.\n\nNathan: Golf clubs, peanut M&M's and a Tide pen.\n\nQ: What is your best and/or worst vacation memory?\n\nNathan: Best vacation memory is any summer I get to spend with my family on tour in fun cities. Worst vacation memory is getting sunburned so bad in Australia that my skin came off when I took off my socks.\n\n(Jae-Ha Kim is a New York Times bestselling author and travel writer. You can respond to this column by visiting her website at www.jaehakim.com. You may also follow \"Go Away With...\" on Twitter at @GoAwayWithJae where Jae-Ha Kim welcomes your questions and comments.)\n\nLove\n\n0\n\nFunny\n\n0\n\nWow\n\n0\n\nSad\n\n0\n\nAngry\n\n0\n\nTags Right after Nathan and I met, I told him that I was leaving on a three-week family hiking trip through southern Utah. I was very difficult to get in touch with during that time. I think that is when he really fell for me! Nathan and I love exploring the Caribbean together. Our power move is tagging on a bonus holiday at the tail end of a big European tour before heading home.\n\nQ: Where have you traveled to for work that you went back to on a personal trip?\n\nNathan: We played the BottleRock Napa Valley [festival] and unfortunately had to fly in and out, but I always knew that I would go back and explore at some point. My wife and I were fortunate enough to make that happen with an amazing adults-only trip for her birthday.\n\nQ: Nathan, do you recall how you felt watching one of Jessie's shows?\n\nNathan: One of my favorite memories was running 10 blocks across Austin in high-heel boots after my set at SXSW so I could catch her set, and all I could think was, \"I hope I don't stink when I hug her after.\" She was a ball of expression and freedom that seemed like she didn't have a care in the world. I immediately gave her an\"I'm with the drummer\" T-shirt.\n\nQ: Are your children good travelers?\n\nJessie: Violet is a pro, Oliver is less so. [Laughs] He is a pandemic baby, so still a bit feral. But this past year, he's gotten the hang of it.\n\nNathan: As long as there is Wi-Fi, but, yes, they do enjoy it. We are blessed with very curious kids who are adaptive to Mommy and Daddy's lifestyle. Violet has more passport stamps than both my parents combined.\n\nQ: Which of you is the more efficient packer?\n\nJessie: One hundred percent me. I outfit plan and very rarely overpack.\n\nNathan: I'm a gypsy. My nickname is Piles, but I somehow always know where everything is.\n\nQ: What untapped destination should people know about?\n\nJessie: I'm very hesitant to share it because it is our paradise, but we love the Dominican Republic. It has some of the most beautiful beaches in the world and is rich with experiences. I love everything about it.\n\nNathan: Mine would be Copenhagen and Denmark, because every time you visit, you can have a totally different experience based on how basic or adventurous you want to be, especially with food.\n\nQ: What is your favorite vacation destination?\n\nJessie: This is difficult, but I have to say Italy. It is just such a beautiful country, and each region holds such magic and is different from the next.\n\nNathan: Dominican Republic. The people, the beaches, the golf and seeing how much joy it brings my kids.\n\nQ: What was a trip you took as a child that stands out?\n\nJessie: Santa Fe. I remember it vividly - the smell of pi\u00f1on wood, going to White Sands, the sound of the bats in the caverns, coyotes howling, eating fry bread from a stand in the middle of the desert. I totally fell for the Southwest forever on that trip. I was five.\n\nNathan: Our family reunion every year in the Tater Hills of Oklahoma where for one weekend a year, mosquito bites were currency.\n\nQ: What's the most important thing you've learned from your travels?\n\nJessie: Have your doctor call in a \"god forbid\" pack of medications.\n\nNathan: Always pack at least two outfits and your basics in your carry-on, and travel in something you could wear to dinner in a pinch.\n\nQ: If you could only pick one place to eat, would you prefer a food truck or fine dining?\n\nJessie: I love a food truck, but I don't love eating standing up or sitting on the curb. I prefer to enjoy a long thoughtful meal, though it doesn't have to necessarily be fancy. I'm going with fine dining.\n\nNathan: Give me a Frito pie and root beer from a truck and I'm one happy camper.\n\nQ: Where are your favorite weekend getaways?\n\nJessie: It would be a tie between Birmingham, Alabama, and Highlands, North Carolina.\n\nNathan: Charleston is 90 minutes door-to-door flight time and my dearest friends Luke and Lauren live there and are always down to show us where the locals like to eat.\n\nQ: What are your five favorite cities?\n\nJessie: Copenhagen, Zurich, London, Barcelona and Rio.\n\nNathan: Milan, Barcelona, Sydney, London and Singapore.\n\nQ: When you go away, what are some of your must-have items?\n\nJessie: Curling iron, journal and travel steamer.\n\nNathan: Golf clubs, peanut M&M's and a Tide pen.\n\nQ: What is your best and/or worst vacation memory?\n\nNathan: Best vacation memory is any summer I get to spend with my family on tour in fun cities. Worst vacation memory is getting sunburned so bad in Australia that my skin came off when I took off my socks.\n\n(Jae-Ha Kim is a New York Times bestselling author and travel writer. Jessie Baylin and Nathan Followill", "body": "Jae-Ha Kim, Tribune Content Agency\n\nFor solo artist Jessie Baylin and Kings of Leon drummer Nathan Followill, this is an especially busy period for the married couple. In May, the Grammy Award-winning Kings of Leon released their latest album \"Can We Please Have Fun.\" And Baylin's May 31 re-release of her critically acclaimed 2018 album \"Strawberry Wind\" - \"Strawberry Wind (Deluxe Edition)\" - also includes new tracks. But with two young children, the musicians are mindful of making sure that one of them is at home with the kids. \"As of right now, I am not going to tour while the Kings are out,\" Baylin said. \"That could change, but I think right now the balance of having one of us home doing the routine with the kids is best.\" Baylin and Followill did this interview from their Nashville home. You may follow them on Instagram (@jezziebaylin and @thenathanfollowill) and X (@doctorfollowill). This interview has been edited for clarity and length.\n\nQ: Do you work on your material at home or on the road or both?\n\nPeople are also reading... UPDATED WITH ADDITIONAL ROADS: Black Hawk County announces road closures due to flooding Hundreds of cars gear up for Waterloo's nostalgic Fourth Street Cruise Man crashes vintage replica hot rod into Waterloo library moments after purchase Waterloo man injured in accidental shooting while cleaning handgun MasterBrand will acquire Bertch parent company Supreme Cabinetry Brands College Square Theatre ends run Thursday, leaving vacancy in College Square Mall Hy-Vee offers measures to help those affected by Logan Avenue store closing Police investigating after security guard brought gun to school dance Waterloo holding annual Memorial Day Parade Patrie found guilty in fatal 2012 Nashua robbery High School Girls Golf: First-round results from state tournament Shared journey: Cedar Falls seniors earn Scouting's highest rank together Police investigate Friday morning gunfire in Waterloo; no injuries reported Waterloo residents angered by Logan Avenue Hy-Vee closure Update: Damaging storms expected in Nebraska and Iowa Saturday night\n\nJessie: All the original material on \"Strawberry Wind\" was written in Nashville over the course of a month - during the strawberry season. The new songs on the deluxe edition were also written while in town this past fall. I think I work best when I'm in the stillness of our home, though.\n\nQ: Jessie, can you share some of your memories of touring with Stevie Nicks?\n\nJessie: Opening for Stevie has been at the top of my mountain of dreams. It has been surreal. The crowds have been kind to me and have really taken in the music and I just love being in her vortex. She truly is one of the most generous of spirit people I have ever known. I love her very much.\n\nQ: When you're not touring, do you prefer to stay at home or take another trip?\n\nNathan: I'm a bit of a homebody. But I also live on a golf course, so I'm happy anywhere that I can get out and chase the little white ball around.\n\nQ: What are some travel memories you'd like to share?\n\nJessie: My parents are wanderlust people, so traveling was a part of my childhood. It wasn't often fancy, but we explored whenever we could. Growing up in New Jersey, the whole eastern coastline was our playground. We would spend time down at the Jersey Shore. Our favorite spot to spend a week every summer was Block Island, Rhode Island. My mom loves the Southwest and her life goal has always been to visit every national park. Right after Nathan and I met, I told him that I was leaving on a three-week family hiking trip through southern Utah. I was very difficult to get in touch with during that time. I think that is when he really fell for me! Nathan and I love exploring the Caribbean together. Our power move is tagging on a bonus holiday at the tail end of a big European tour before heading home.\n\nQ: Where have you traveled to for work that you went back to on a personal trip?\n\nNathan: We played the BottleRock Napa Valley [festival] and unfortunately had to fly in and out, but I always knew that I would go back and explore at some point. My wife and I were fortunate enough to make that happen with an amazing adults-only trip for her birthday.\n\nQ: Nathan, do you recall how you felt watching one of Jessie's shows?\n\nNathan: One of my favorite memories was running 10 blocks across Austin in high-heel boots after my set at SXSW so I could catch her set, and all I could think was, \"I hope I don't stink when I hug her after.\" She was a ball of expression and freedom that seemed like she didn't have a care in the world. I immediately gave her an\"I'm with the drummer\" T-shirt.\n\nQ: Are your children good travelers?\n\nJessie: Violet is a pro, Oliver is less so. [Laughs] He is a pandemic baby, so still a bit feral. But this past year, he's gotten the hang of it.\n\nNathan: As long as there is Wi-Fi, but, yes, they do enjoy it. We are blessed with very curious kids who are adaptive to Mommy and Daddy's lifestyle. Violet has more passport stamps than both my parents combined.\n\nQ: Which of you is the more efficient packer?\n\nJessie: One hundred percent me. I outfit plan and very rarely overpack.\n\nNathan: I'm a gypsy. My nickname is Piles, but I somehow always know where everything is.\n\nQ: What untapped destination should people know about?\n\nJessie: I'm very hesitant to share it because it is our paradise, but we love the Dominican Republic. It has some of the most beautiful beaches in the world and is rich with experiences. I love everything about it.\n\nNathan: Mine would be Copenhagen and Denmark, because every time you visit, you can have a totally different experience based on how basic or adventurous you want to be, especially with food.\n\nQ: What is your favorite vacation destination?\n\nJessie: This is difficult, but I have to say Italy. It is just such a beautiful country, and each region holds such magic and is different from the next.\n\nNathan: Dominican Republic. The people, the beaches, the golf and seeing how much joy it brings my kids.\n\nQ: What was a trip you took as a child that stands out?\n\nJessie: Santa Fe. I remember it vividly - the smell of pi\u00f1on wood, going to White Sands, the sound of the bats in the caverns, coyotes howling, eating fry bread from a stand in the middle of the desert. I totally fell for the Southwest forever on that trip. I was five.\n\nNathan: Our family reunion every year in the Tater Hills of Oklahoma where for one weekend a year, mosquito bites were currency.\n\nQ: What's the most important thing you've learned from your travels?\n\nJessie: Have your doctor call in a \"god forbid\" pack of medications.\n\nNathan: Always pack at least two outfits and your basics in your carry-on, and travel in something you could wear to dinner in a pinch.\n\nQ: If you could only pick one place to eat, would you prefer a food truck or fine dining?\n\nJessie: I love a food truck, but I don't love eating standing up or sitting on the curb. I prefer to enjoy a long thoughtful meal, though it doesn't have to necessarily be fancy. I'm going with fine dining.\n\nNathan: Give me a Frito pie and root beer from a truck and I'm one happy camper.\n\nQ: Where are your favorite weekend getaways?\n\nJessie: It would be a tie between Birmingham, Alabama, and Highlands, North Carolina.\n\nNathan: Charleston is 90 minutes door-to-door flight time and my dearest friends Luke and Lauren live there and are always down to show us where the locals like to eat.\n\nQ: What are your five favorite cities?\n\nJessie: Copenhagen, Zurich, London, Barcelona and Rio.\n\nNathan: Milan, Barcelona, Sydney, London and Singapore.\n\nQ: When you go away, what are some of your must-have items?\n\nJessie: Curling iron, journal and travel steamer.\n\nNathan: Golf clubs, peanut M&M's and a Tide pen.\n\nQ: What is your best and/or worst vacation memory?\n\nNathan: Best vacation memory is any summer I get to spend with my family on tour in fun cities. Worst vacation memory is getting sunburned so bad in Australia that my skin came off when I took off my socks.\n\n(Jae-Ha Kim is a New York Times bestselling author and travel writer. {"uri": "8149167482", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-05-28", "time": "05:31:27", "dateTime": "2024-05-28T05:31:27Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-05-28T05:30:39Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.9176470637321472, "url": "https://richmond.com/life-entertainment/nation-world/travel/go-away-with-jessie-baylin-and-nathan-followill/article_3cc67f3b-e218-5ebc-900f-a60e809921b6.html", "title": "Go away with ... Jessie Baylin and Nathan Followill", "body": "Jae-Ha Kim, Tribune Content Agency\n\nFor solo artist Jessie Baylin and Kings of Leon drummer Nathan Followill, this is an especially busy period for the married couple. In May, the Grammy Award-winning Kings of Leon released their latest album \"Can We Please Have Fun.\" And Baylin's May 31 re-release of her critically acclaimed 2018 album \"Strawberry Wind\" - \"Strawberry Wind (Deluxe Edition)\" - also includes new tracks. But with two young children, the musicians are mindful of making sure that one of them is at home with the kids. \"As of right now, I am not going to tour while the Kings are out,\" Baylin said. \"That could change, but I think right now the balance of having one of us home doing the routine with the kids is best.\" Baylin and Followill did this interview from their Nashville home. You may follow them on Instagram (@jezziebaylin and @thenathanfollowill) and X (@doctorfollowill). This interview has been edited for clarity and length.\n\nQ: Do you work on your material at home or on the road or both?\n\nPeople are also reading... Wyclef Jean, Fantasia, Ludacris to perform at Richmond Jazz Festival Richmond plans to build $150,000 kids nature zone on Belle Isle Richmond Coliseum demolition on pause, could start in 2025 High school spring playoffs: VHSL bracket updates for baseball, softball, soccer, lacrosse Chesterfield has a new ice cream flavor VCU hoops star guard Shulga returning to Rams in massive coup for Odom Youngkin's plan to vacate James Monroe Building on hold Richmond's convention center is often empty. A hotel will fix that, leaders say. 5 Va. colleges awarded lab school funding must resubmit applications Amid brain cancer battle, Kristen Wommack honored by Deep Run teammates Legend Brewing Co. could sell its building or business RPS marks renaming of George Wythe as Richmond High School for the Arts Richmond plans to sell Arthur Ashe Center, give proceeds to school system Inflation wallops Richmond restaurants, customers VCU won't directly pay its athletes, though new state law allows it\n\nJessie: All the original material on \"Strawberry Wind\" was written in Nashville over the course of a month - during the strawberry season. The new songs on the deluxe edition were also written while in town this past fall. I think I work best when I'm in the stillness of our home, though.\n\nQ: Jessie, can you share some of your memories of touring with Stevie Nicks?\n\nJessie: Opening for Stevie has been at the top of my mountain of dreams. It has been surreal. The crowds have been kind to me and have really taken in the music and I just love being in her vortex. She truly is one of the most generous of spirit people I have ever known. I love her very much.\n\nQ: When you're not touring, do you prefer to stay at home or take another trip?\n\nNathan: I'm a bit of a homebody. But I also live on a golf course, so I'm happy anywhere that I can get out and chase the little white ball around.\n\nQ: What are some travel memories you'd like to share?\n\nJessie: My parents are wanderlust people, so traveling was a part of my childhood. It wasn't often fancy, but we explored whenever we could. Growing up in New Jersey, the whole eastern coastline was our playground. We would spend time down at the Jersey Shore. Our favorite spot to spend a week every summer was Block Island, Rhode Island. My mom loves the Southwest and her life goal has always been to visit every national park. Right after Nathan and I met, I told him that I was leaving on a three-week family hiking trip through southern Utah. I was very difficult to get in touch with during that time. I think that is when he really fell for me! Nathan and I love exploring the Caribbean together. Our power move is tagging on a bonus holiday at the tail end of a big European tour before heading home.\n\nQ: Where have you traveled to for work that you went back to on a personal trip?\n\nNathan: We played the BottleRock Napa Valley [festival] and unfortunately had to fly in and out, but I always knew that I would go back and explore at some point. My wife and I were fortunate enough to make that happen with an amazing adults-only trip for her birthday.\n\nQ: Nathan, do you recall how you felt watching one of Jessie's shows?\n\nNathan: One of my favorite memories was running 10 blocks across Austin in high-heel boots after my set at SXSW so I could catch her set, and all I could think was, \"I hope I don't stink when I hug her after.\" She was a ball of expression and freedom that seemed like she didn't have a care in the world. I immediately gave her an\"I'm with the drummer\" T-shirt.\n\nQ: Are your children good travelers?\n\nJessie: Violet is a pro, Oliver is less so. [Laughs] He is a pandemic baby, so still a bit feral. But this past year, he's gotten the hang of it.\n\nNathan: As long as there is Wi-Fi, but, yes, they do enjoy it. We are blessed with very curious kids who are adaptive to Mommy and Daddy's lifestyle. Violet has more passport stamps than both my parents combined.\n\nQ: Which of you is the more efficient packer?\n\nJessie: One hundred percent me. I outfit plan and very rarely overpack.\n\nNathan: I'm a gypsy. My nickname is Piles, but I somehow always know where everything is.\n\nQ: What untapped destination should people know about?\n\nJessie: I'm very hesitant to share it because it is our paradise, but we love the Dominican Republic. It has some of the most beautiful beaches in the world and is rich with experiences. I love everything about it.\n\nNathan: Mine would be Copenhagen and Denmark, because every time you visit, you can have a totally different experience based on how basic or adventurous you want to be, especially with food.\n\nQ: What is your favorite vacation destination?\n\nJessie: This is difficult, but I have to say Italy. It is just such a beautiful country, and each region holds such magic and is different from the next.\n\nNathan: Dominican Republic. The people, the beaches, the golf and seeing how much joy it brings my kids.\n\nQ: What was a trip you took as a child that stands out?\n\nJessie: Santa Fe. I remember it vividly - the smell of pi\u00f1on wood, going to White Sands, the sound of the bats in the caverns, coyotes howling, eating fry bread from a stand in the middle of the desert. I totally fell for the Southwest forever on that trip. I was five.\n\nNathan: Our family reunion every year in the Tater Hills of Oklahoma where for one weekend a year, mosquito bites were currency.\n\nQ: What's the most important thing you've learned from your travels?\n\nJessie: Have your doctor call in a \"god forbid\" pack of medications.\n\nNathan: Always pack at least two outfits and your basics in your carry-on, and travel in something you could wear to dinner in a pinch.\n\nQ: If you could only pick one place to eat, would you prefer a food truck or fine dining?\n\nJessie: I love a food truck, but I don't love eating standing up or sitting on the curb. I prefer to enjoy a long thoughtful meal, though it doesn't have to necessarily be fancy. I'm going with fine dining.\n\nNathan: Give me a Frito pie and root beer from a truck and I'm one happy camper.\n\nQ: Where are your favorite weekend getaways?\n\nJessie: It would be a tie between Birmingham, Alabama, and Highlands, North Carolina.\n\nNathan: Charleston is 90 minutes door-to-door flight time and my dearest friends Luke and Lauren live there and are always down to show us where the locals like to eat.\n\nQ: What are your five favorite cities?\n\nJessie: Copenhagen, Zurich, London, Barcelona and Rio.\n\nNathan: Milan, Barcelona, Sydney, London and Singapore.\n\nQ: When you go away, what are some of your must-have items?\n\nJessie: Curling iron, journal and travel steamer.\n\nNathan: Golf clubs, peanut M&M's and a Tide pen.\n\nQ: What is your best and/or worst vacation memory?\n\nNathan: Best vacation memory is any summer I get to spend with my family on tour in fun cities. Worst vacation memory is getting sunburned so bad in Australia that my skin came off when I took off my socks.\n\n(Jae-Ha Kim is a New York Times bestselling author and travel writer. You can respond to this column by visiting her website at www.jaehakim.com. You may also follow \"Go Away With...\" on Twitter at @GoAwayWithJae where Jae-Ha Kim welcomes your questions and comments.)\n\nTags Dcc Easytravel101 Wire Tns Travel", "source": {"uri": {"uri": "8149153865", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-05-28", "time": "05:18:53", "dateTime": "2024-05-28T05:18:53Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-05-28T05:18:09Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.9137254953384399, "url": "https://tucson.com/life-entertainment/nation-world/travel/go-away-with-jessie-baylin-and-nathan-followill/article_14c5b71e-2155-55ba-a276-e95e7340926c.html", "title": "Go away with ... Jessie Baylin and Nathan Followill", "body": "Jae-Ha Kim, Tribune Content Agency\n\nFor solo artist Jessie Baylin and Kings of Leon drummer Nathan Followill, this is an especially busy period for the married couple. In May, the Grammy Award-winning Kings of Leon released their latest album \"Can We Please Have Fun.\" And Baylin's May 31 re-release of her critically acclaimed 2018 album \"Strawberry Wind\" - \"Strawberry Wind (Deluxe Edition)\" - also includes new tracks. But with two young children, the musicians are mindful of making sure that one of them is at home with the kids. \"As of right now, I am not going to tour while the Kings are out,\" Baylin said. \"That could change, but I think right now the balance of having one of us home doing the routine with the kids is best.\" Baylin and Followill did this interview from their Nashville home. You may follow them on Instagram (@jezziebaylin and @thenathanfollowill) and X (@doctorfollowill). This interview has been edited for clarity and length.\n\nQ: Do you work on your material at home or on the road or both?\n\nPeople are also reading... Iconic Tucson Mexican restaurant could face the wrecking ball 12 Tucson restaurants that have closed their doors this year \ud83d\ude25 33 fun events happening in Tucson this weekend May 23-26 \ud83d\udd7a\ud83d\udecd Popular Japanese dollar store Daiso is opening its first Tucson location Ironwood bloom among best in years: Desert's 'grand old man' is dressed in pink Saguaros are blooming! 8 facts about saguaro blossoms City crews start clearing part of Tucson's biggest homeless camp Tucson woman arrested after fight with teen girl at high school graduation U of A may now have to pay athletes $20 million annually amid college sports restructuring Condo project's success not spurring new development in Tucson despite housing shortage Off limits except to ghosts: Ruby townsite will soon be closed to tourists Hansen's notebook: Arizona's Reed-Francois off to promising start as new ASU AD Rossini has catching up to do Jewel's Noodle Kitchen is a hidden gem and it deserves all the attention Arizona coach Tommy Lloyd says Anthony Dell'Orso to bring versatility to Wildcats Casa Molina on Speedway could face the wrecking ball\n\nJessie: All the original material on \"Strawberry Wind\" was written in Nashville over the course of a month - during the strawberry season. The new songs on the deluxe edition were also written while in town this past fall. I think I work best when I'm in the stillness of our home, though.\n\nQ: Jessie, can you share some of your memories of touring with Stevie Nicks?\n\nJessie: Opening for Stevie has been at the top of my mountain of dreams. It has been surreal. The crowds have been kind to me and have really taken in the music and I just love being in her vortex. She truly is one of the most generous of spirit people I have ever known. I love her very much.\n\nQ: When you're not touring, do you prefer to stay at home or take another trip?\n\nNathan: I'm a bit of a homebody. But I also live on a golf course, so I'm happy anywhere that I can get out and chase the little white ball around.\n\nQ: What are some travel memories you'd like to share?\n\nJessie: My parents are wanderlust people, so traveling was a part of my childhood. It wasn't often fancy, but we explored whenever we could. Growing up in New Jersey, the whole eastern coastline was our playground. We would spend time down at the Jersey Shore. Our favorite spot to spend a week every summer was Block Island, Rhode Island. My mom loves the Southwest and her life goal has always been to visit every national park. Right after Nathan and I met, I told him that I was leaving on a three-week family hiking trip through southern Utah. I was very difficult to get in touch with during that time. I think that is when he really fell for me! Nathan and I love exploring the Caribbean together. Our power move is tagging on a bonus holiday at the tail end of a big European tour before heading home.\n\nQ: Where have you traveled to for work that you went back to on a personal trip?\n\nNathan: We played the BottleRock Napa Valley [festival] and unfortunately had to fly in and out, but I always knew that I would go back and explore at some point. My wife and I were fortunate enough to make that happen with an amazing adults-only trip for her birthday.\n\nQ: Nathan, do you recall how you felt watching one of Jessie's shows?\n\nNathan: One of my favorite memories was running 10 blocks across Austin in high-heel boots after my set at SXSW so I could catch her set, and all I could think was, \"I hope I don't stink when I hug her after.\" She was a ball of expression and freedom that seemed like she didn't have a care in the world. I immediately gave her an\"I'm with the drummer\" T-shirt.\n\nQ: Are your children good travelers?\n\nJessie: Violet is a pro, Oliver is less so. [Laughs] He is a pandemic baby, so still a bit feral. But this past year, he's gotten the hang of it.\n\nNathan: As long as there is Wi-Fi, but, yes, they do enjoy it. We are blessed with very curious kids who are adaptive to Mommy and Daddy's lifestyle. Violet has more passport stamps than both my parents combined.\n\nQ: Which of you is the more efficient packer?\n\nJessie: One hundred percent me. I outfit plan and very rarely overpack.\n\nNathan: I'm a gypsy. My nickname is Piles, but I somehow always know where everything is.\n\nQ: What untapped destination should people know about?\n\nJessie: I'm very hesitant to share it because it is our paradise, but we love the Dominican Republic. It has some of the most beautiful beaches in the world and is rich with experiences. I love everything about it.\n\nNathan: Mine would be Copenhagen and Denmark, because every time you visit, you can have a totally different experience based on how basic or adventurous you want to be, especially with food.\n\nQ: What is your favorite vacation destination?\n\nJessie: This is difficult, but I have to say Italy. It is just such a beautiful country, and each region holds such magic and is different from the next.\n\nNathan: Dominican Republic. The people, the beaches, the golf and seeing how much joy it brings my kids.\n\nQ: What was a trip you took as a child that stands out?\n\nJessie: Santa Fe. I remember it vividly - the smell of pi\u00f1on wood, going to White Sands, the sound of the bats in the caverns, coyotes howling, eating fry bread from a stand in the middle of the desert. I totally fell for the Southwest forever on that trip. I was five.\n\nNathan: Our family reunion every year in the Tater Hills of Oklahoma where for one weekend a year, mosquito bites were currency.\n\nQ: What's the most important thing you've learned from your travels?\n\nJessie: Have your doctor call in a \"god forbid\" pack of medications.\n\nNathan: Always pack at least two outfits and your basics in your carry-on, and travel in something you could wear to dinner in a pinch.\n\nQ: If you could only pick one place to eat, would you prefer a food truck or fine dining?\n\nJessie: I love a food truck, but I don't love eating standing up or sitting on the curb. I prefer to enjoy a long thoughtful meal, though it doesn't have to necessarily be fancy. I'm going with fine dining.\n\nNathan: Give me a Frito pie and root beer from a truck and I'm one happy camper.\n\nQ: Where are your favorite weekend getaways?\n\nJessie: It would be a tie between Birmingham, Alabama, and Highlands, North Carolina.\n\nNathan: Charleston is 90 minutes door-to-door flight time and my dearest friends Luke and Lauren live there and are always down to show us where the locals like to eat.\n\nQ: What are your five favorite cities?\n\nJessie: Copenhagen, Zurich, London, Barcelona and Rio.\n\nNathan: Milan, Barcelona, Sydney, London and Singapore.\n\nQ: When you go away, what are some of your must-have items?\n\nJessie: Curling iron, journal and travel steamer.\n\nNathan: Golf clubs, peanut M&M's and a Tide pen.\n\nQ: What is your best and/or worst vacation memory?\n\nNathan: Best vacation memory is any summer I get to spend with my family on tour in fun cities. Worst vacation memory is getting sunburned so bad in Australia that my skin came off when I took off my socks.\n\n(Jae-Ha Kim is a New York Times bestselling author and travel writer. You can respond to this column by visiting her website at www.jaehakim.com. I totally fell for the Southwest forever on that trip. I was five.\n\nNathan: Our family reunion every year in the Tater Hills of Oklahoma where for one weekend a year, mosquito bites were currency.\n\nQ: What's the most important thing you've learned from your travels?\n\nJessie: Have your doctor call in a \"god forbid\" pack of medications.\n\nNathan: Always pack at least two outfits and your basics in your carry-on, and travel in something you could wear to dinner in a pinch.\n\nQ: If you could only pick one place to eat, would you prefer a food truck or fine dining?\n\nJessie: I love a food truck, but I don't love eating standing up or sitting on the curb. I prefer to enjoy a long thoughtful meal, though it doesn't have to necessarily be fancy. I'm going with fine dining.\n\nNathan: Give me a Frito pie and root beer from a truck and I'm one happy camper.\n\nQ: Where are your favorite weekend getaways?\n\nJessie: It would be a tie between Birmingham, Alabama, and Highlands, North Carolina.\n\nNathan: Charleston is 90 minutes door-to-door flight time and my dearest friends Luke and Lauren live there and are always down to show us where the locals like to eat.\n\nQ: What are your five favorite cities?\n\nJessie: Copenhagen, Zurich, London, Barcelona and Rio.\n\nNathan: Milan, Barcelona, Sydney, London and Singapore.\n\nQ: When you go away, what are some of your must-have items?\n\nJessie: Curling iron, journal and travel steamer.\n\nNathan: Golf clubs, peanut M&M's and a Tide pen.\n\nQ: What is your best and/or worst vacation memory?\n\nNathan: Best vacation memory is any summer I get to spend with my family on tour in fun cities. Worst vacation memory is getting sunburned so bad in Australia that my skin came off when I took off my socks.\n\n(Jae-Ha Kim is a New York Times bestselling author and travel writer.
