{"uri": "8149155037", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-05-28", "time": "05:19:45", "dateTime": "2024-05-28T05:19:45Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-05-28T05:19:02Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.9058823585510254, "url": "https://scnow.com/life-entertainment/nation-world/travel/go-away-with-jessie-baylin-and-nathan-followill/article_15c6461b-4b3b-5782-8171-59dacd3e7dc8.html", "title": "Go away with ... Jessie Baylin and Nathan Followill", "body": "Jae-Ha Kim, Tribune Content Agency\n\nFor solo artist Jessie Baylin and Kings of Leon drummer Nathan Followill, this is an especially busy period for the married couple. In May, the Grammy Award-winning Kings of Leon released their latest album \"Can We Please Have Fun.\" And Baylin's May 31 re-release of her critically acclaimed 2018 album \"Strawberry Wind\" - \"Strawberry Wind (Deluxe Edition)\" - also includes new tracks. But with two young children, the musicians are mindful of making sure that one of them is at home with the kids. \"As of right now, I am not going to tour while the Kings are out,\" Baylin said. \"That could change, but I think right now the balance of having one of us home doing the routine with the kids is best.\" Baylin and Followill did this interview from their Nashville home. You may follow them on Instagram (@jezziebaylin and @thenathanfollowill) and X (@doctorfollowill). This interview has been edited for clarity and length.\n\nQ: Do you work on your material at home or on the road or both?\n\nPeople are also reading... Kevin Robinson won't return as West Florence boys' basketball coach New warrant scam targets Florence County residents Florence County deputies serve warrant, find guns and drugs One arrested, one sought in Florence gun store burglary FDTC baseball cruises to 1st win in JUCO World Series SLED to investigate Florence County deputy involved shooting New Florence mental health facility 'tops out' Col. Erika Perry to speak at Florence Memorial Day ceremony West Florence softball finishes as 4A state runner-up West Florence softball looks ahead to Game 2 of state finals Mother-daughter, husband-wife died in SC crash Stokes set to participate in Miss S.C. competition Wilson tabs former Hartsville coach English to take over boys basketball program Under new ownership, Flamingos roll past Macon in season opener Hartsville Chamber serves power for breakfast\n\nJessie: All the original material on \"Strawberry Wind\" was written in Nashville over the course of a month - during the strawberry season. The new songs on the deluxe edition were also written while in town this past fall. I think I work best when I'm in the stillness of our home, though.\n\nQ: Jessie, can you share some of your memories of touring with Stevie Nicks?\n\nJessie: Opening for Stevie has been at the top of my mountain of dreams. It has been surreal. The crowds have been kind to me and have really taken in the music and I just love being in her vortex. She truly is one of the most generous of spirit people I have ever known. I love her very much.\n\nQ: When you're not touring, do you prefer to stay at home or take another trip?\n\nNathan: I'm a bit of a homebody. But I also live on a golf course, so I'm happy anywhere that I can get out and chase the little white ball around.\n\nQ: What are some travel memories you'd like to share?\n\nJessie: My parents are wanderlust people, so traveling was a part of my childhood. It wasn't often fancy, but we explored whenever we could. Growing up in New Jersey, the whole eastern coastline was our playground. We would spend time down at the Jersey Shore. Our favorite spot to spend a week every summer was Block Island, Rhode Island. My mom loves the Southwest and her life goal has always been to visit every national park. Right after Nathan and I met, I told him that I was leaving on a three-week family hiking trip through southern Utah. I was very difficult to get in touch with during that time. I think that is when he really fell for me! Nathan and I love exploring the Caribbean together. Our power move is tagging on a bonus holiday at the tail end of a big European tour before heading home.\n\nQ: Where have you traveled to for work that you went back to on a personal trip?\n\nNathan: We played the BottleRock Napa Valley [festival] and unfortunately had to fly in and out, but I always knew that I would go back and explore at some point. My wife and I were fortunate enough to make that happen with an amazing adults-only trip for her birthday.\n\nQ: Nathan, do you recall how you felt watching one of Jessie's shows?\n\nNathan: One of my favorite memories was running 10 blocks across Austin in high-heel boots after my set at SXSW so I could catch her set, and all I could think was, \"I hope I don't stink when I hug her after.\" She was a ball of expression and freedom that seemed like she didn't have a care in the world. I immediately gave her an\"I'm with the drummer\" T-shirt.\n\nQ: Are your children good travelers?\n\nJessie: Violet is a pro, Oliver is less so. [Laughs] He is a pandemic baby, so still a bit feral. But this past year, he's gotten the hang of it.\n\nNathan: As long as there is Wi-Fi, but, yes, they do enjoy it. We are blessed with very curious kids who are adaptive to Mommy and Daddy's lifestyle. Violet has more passport stamps than both my parents combined.\n\nQ: Which of you is the more efficient packer?\n\nJessie: One hundred percent me. I outfit plan and very rarely overpack.\n\nNathan: I'm a gypsy. My nickname is Piles, but I somehow always know where everything is.\n\nQ: What untapped destination should people know about?\n\nJessie: I'm very hesitant to share it because it is our paradise, but we love the Dominican Republic. It has some of the most beautiful beaches in the world and is rich with experiences. I love everything about it.\n\nNathan: Mine would be Copenhagen and Denmark, because every time you visit, you can have a totally different experience based on how basic or adventurous you want to be, especially with food.\n\nQ: What is your favorite vacation destination?\n\nJessie: This is difficult, but I have to say Italy. It is just such a beautiful country, and each region holds such magic and is different from the next.\n\nNathan: Dominican Republic. The people, the beaches, the golf and seeing how much joy it brings my kids.\n\nQ: What was a trip you took as a child that stands out?\n\nJessie: Santa Fe. I remember it vividly - the smell of pi\u00f1on wood, going to White Sands, the sound of the bats in the caverns, coyotes howling, eating fry bread from a stand in the middle of the desert. I totally fell for the Southwest forever on that trip. I was five.\n\nNathan: Our family reunion every year in the Tater Hills of Oklahoma where for one weekend a year, mosquito bites were currency.\n\nQ: What's the most important thing you've learned from your travels?\n\nJessie: Have your doctor call in a \"god forbid\" pack of medications.\n\nNathan: Always pack at least two outfits and your basics in your carry-on, and travel in something you could wear to dinner in a pinch.\n\nQ: If you could only pick one place to eat, would you prefer a food truck or fine dining?\n\nJessie: I love a food truck, but I don't love eating standing up or sitting on the curb. I prefer to enjoy a long thoughtful meal, though it doesn't have to necessarily be fancy. I'm going with fine dining.\n\nNathan: Give me a Frito pie and root beer from a truck and I'm one happy camper.\n\nQ: Where are your favorite weekend getaways?\n\nJessie: It would be a tie between Birmingham, Alabama, and Highlands, North Carolina.\n\nNathan: Charleston is 90 minutes door-to-door flight time and my dearest friends Luke and Lauren live there and are always down to show us where the locals like to eat.\n\nQ: What are your five favorite cities?\n\nJessie: Copenhagen, Zurich, London, Barcelona and Rio.\n\nNathan: Milan, Barcelona, Sydney, London and Singapore.\n\nQ: When you go away, what are some of your must-have items?\n\nJessie: Curling iron, journal and travel steamer.\n\nNathan: Golf clubs, peanut M&M's and a Tide pen.\n\nQ: What is your best and/or worst vacation memory?\n\nNathan: Best vacation memory is any summer I get to spend with my family on tour in fun cities. Worst vacation memory is getting sunburned so bad in Australia that my skin came off when I took off my socks.\n\n(Jae-Ha Kim is a New York Times bestselling author and travel writer. {"uri": "2024-05-370364288", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-05-28", "time": "05:08:29", "dateTime": "2024-05-28T05:08:29Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-05-28T04:00:00Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.9058823585510254, "url": "https://missoulian.com/life-entertainment/nation-world/travel/go-away-with-jessie-baylin-and-nathan-followill/article_e831a53b-e8df-5e45-8065-544015d0591f.html", "title": "Go away with ... Jessie Baylin and Nathan Followill", "body": "Married musicians Jessie Baylin and Nathan Followill said Mexico City and anywhere in Thailand are on their travel bucket lists.\n\nJae-Ha Kim, Tribune Content Agency\n\nFor solo artist Jessie Baylin and Kings of Leon drummer Nathan Followill, this is an especially busy period for the married couple. In May, the Grammy Award-winning Kings of Leon released their latest album \"Can We Please Have Fun.\" And Baylin's May 31 re-release of her critically acclaimed 2018 album \"Strawberry Wind\" - \"Strawberry Wind (Deluxe Edition)\" - also includes new tracks. But with two young children, the musicians are mindful of making sure that one of them is at home with the kids. \"As of right now, I am not going to tour while the Kings are out,\" Baylin said. \"That could change, but I think right now the balance of having one of us home doing the routine with the kids is best.\" Baylin and Followill did this interview from their Nashville home. You may follow them on Instagram (@jezziebaylin and @thenathanfollowill) and X (@doctorfollowill). This interview has been edited for clarity and length.\n\nQ: Do you work on your material at home or on the road or both?\n\nPeople are also reading...\n\nMontana promoter Logjam cited in Live Nation monopoly case Business Buzz: New restaurant to open, more flights from Missoula Brad Tschida: Missoula fire department levy is unnecessary Here's Montana's snow forecast; winter storm warning for parts of the state Streets around Missoula courthouse to close due to 'Yellowstone' filming Missoula farm owner seeks $310K in Open Space Bond funds for ag preservation UPDATE: Jury finds Cody Marble did not prove innocence at trial Tanner Olson legacy flies high in new Rattlesnake bike park Sheehy skepticism among ultra-Republicans still lingers going into primary Private two-bedroom lakeshore cabin in Glacier National Park listed for $15M Montana shelter providers convene in Missoula to discuss homelessness Eagle Watch Estates residents allege mistreatment, HUD investigating 0 Bedroom Home in Missoula - $1,000,000 Flathead dam cleared to add extra 2 feet of water by Memorial Day Memorial Day weekend events salute Montana's fallen heroes\n\nJessie: All the original material on \"Strawberry Wind\" was written in Nashville over the course of a month - during the strawberry season. The new songs on the deluxe edition were also written while in town this past fall. I think I work best when I'm in the stillness of our home, though.\n\nQ: Jessie, can you share some of your memories of touring with Stevie Nicks?\n\nJessie: Opening for Stevie has been at the top of my mountain of dreams. It has been surreal. The crowds have been kind to me and have really taken in the music and I just love being in her vortex. She truly is one of the most generous of spirit people I have ever known. I love her very much.\n\nQ: When you're not touring, do you prefer to stay at home or take another trip?\n\nNathan: I'm a bit of a homebody. But I also live on a golf course, so I'm happy anywhere that I can get out and chase the little white ball around.\n\nQ: What are some travel memories you'd like to share?\n\nJessie: My parents are wanderlust people, so traveling was a part of my childhood. It wasn't often fancy, but we explored whenever we could. Growing up in New Jersey, the whole eastern coastline was our playground. We would spend time down at the Jersey Shore. Our favorite spot to spend a week every summer was Block Island, Rhode Island. My mom loves the Southwest and her life goal has always been to visit every national park. Right after Nathan and I met, I told him that I was leaving on a three-week family hiking trip through southern Utah. I was very difficult to get in touch with during that time. I think that is when he really fell for me! Nathan and I love exploring the Caribbean together. Our power move is tagging on a bonus holiday at the tail end of a big European tour before heading home.\n\nQ: Where have you traveled to for work that you went back to on a personal trip?\n\nNathan: We played the BottleRock Napa Valley [festival] and unfortunately had to fly in and out, but I always knew that I would go back and explore at some point. My wife and I were fortunate enough to make that happen with an amazing adults-only trip for her birthday.\n\nQ: Nathan, do you recall how you felt watching one of Jessie's shows?\n\nNathan: One of my favorite memories was running 10 blocks across Austin in high-heel boots after my set at SXSW so I could catch her set, and all I could think was, \"I hope I don't stink when I hug her after.\" She was a ball of expression and freedom that seemed like she didn't have a care in the world. I immediately gave her an\"I'm with the drummer\" T-shirt.\n\nQ: Are your children good travelers?\n\nJessie: Violet is a pro, Oliver is less so. [Laughs] He is a pandemic baby, so still a bit feral. But this past year, he's gotten the hang of it.\n\nNathan: As long as there is Wi-Fi, but, yes, they do enjoy it. We are blessed with very curious kids who are adaptive to Mommy and Daddy's lifestyle. Violet has more passport stamps than both my parents combined.\n\nQ: Which of you is the more efficient packer?\n\nJessie: One hundred percent me. I outfit plan and very rarely overpack.\n\nNathan: I'm a gypsy. My nickname is Piles, but I somehow always know where everything is.\n\nQ: What untapped destination should people know about?\n\nJessie: I'm very hesitant to share it because it is our paradise, but we love the Dominican Republic. It has some of the most beautiful beaches in the world and is rich with experiences. I love everything about it.\n\nNathan: Mine would be Copenhagen and Denmark, because every time you visit, you can have a totally different experience based on how basic or adventurous you want to be, especially with food.\n\nQ: What is your favorite vacation destination?\n\nJessie: This is difficult, but I have to say Italy. It is just such a beautiful country, and each region holds such magic and is different from the next.\n\nNathan: Dominican Republic. The people, the beaches, the golf and seeing how much joy it brings my kids.\n\nQ: What was a trip you took as a child that stands out?\n\nJessie: Santa Fe. I remember it vividly - the smell of pi\u00f1on wood, going to White Sands, the sound of the bats in the caverns, coyotes howling, eating fry bread from a stand in the middle of the desert. I totally fell for the Southwest forever on that trip. I was five.\n\nNathan: Our family reunion every year in the Tater Hills of Oklahoma where for one weekend a year, mosquito bites were currency.\n\nQ: What's the most important thing you've learned from your travels?\n\nJessie: Have your doctor call in a \"god forbid\" pack of medications.\n\nNathan: Always pack at least two outfits and your basics in your carry-on, and travel in something you could wear to dinner in a pinch.\n\nQ: If you could only pick one place to eat, would you prefer a food truck or fine dining?\n\nJessie: I love a food truck, but I don't love eating standing up or sitting on the curb. I prefer to enjoy a long thoughtful meal, though it doesn't have to necessarily be fancy. I'm going with fine dining.\n\nNathan: Give me a Frito pie and root beer from a truck and I'm one happy camper.\n\nQ: Where are your favorite weekend getaways?\n\nJessie: It would be a tie between Birmingham, Alabama, and Highlands, North Carolina.\n\nNathan: Charleston is 90 minutes door-to-door flight time and my dearest friends Luke and Lauren live there and are always down to show us where the locals like to eat.\n\nQ: What are your five favorite cities?\n\nJessie: Copenhagen, Zurich, London, Barcelona and Rio.\n\nNathan: Milan, Barcelona, Sydney, London and Singapore.\n\nQ: When you go away, what are some of your must-have items?\n\nJessie: Curling iron, journal and travel steamer.\n\nNathan: Golf clubs, peanut M&M's and a Tide pen.\n\nQ: What is your best and/or worst vacation memory?\n\nNathan: Best vacation memory is any summer I get to spend with my family on tour in fun cities. Worst vacation memory is getting sunburned so bad in Australia that my skin came off when I took off my socks.\n\n(Jae-Ha Kim is a New York Times bestselling author and travel writer. You can respond to this column by visiting her website at www.jaehakim.com. Our favorite spot to spend a week every summer was Block Island, Rhode Island. My mom loves the Southwest and her life goal has always been to visit every national park. Right after Nathan and I met, I told him that I was leaving on a three-week family hiking trip through southern Utah. I was very difficult to get in touch with during that time. I think that is when he really fell for me! Nathan and I love exploring the Caribbean together. Our power move is tagging on a bonus holiday at the tail end of a big European tour before heading home.\n\nQ: Where have you traveled to for work that you went back to on a personal trip?\n\nNathan: We played the BottleRock Napa Valley [festival] and unfortunately had to fly in and out, but I always knew that I would go back and explore at some point. My wife and I were fortunate enough to make that happen with an amazing adults-only trip for her birthday.\n\nQ: Nathan, do you recall how you felt watching one of Jessie's shows?\n\nNathan: One of my favorite memories was running 10 blocks across Austin in high-heel boots after my set at SXSW so I could catch her set, and all I could think was, \"I hope I don't stink when I hug her after.\" She was a ball of expression and freedom that seemed like she didn't have a care in the world. I immediately gave her an\"I'm with the drummer\" T-shirt.\n\nQ: Are your children good travelers?\n\nJessie: Violet is a pro, Oliver is less so. [Laughs] He is a pandemic baby, so still a bit feral. But this past year, he's gotten the hang of it.\n\nNathan: As long as there is Wi-Fi, but, yes, they do enjoy it. We are blessed with very curious kids who are adaptive to Mommy and Daddy's lifestyle. Violet has more passport stamps than both my parents combined.\n\nQ: Which of you is the more efficient packer?\n\nJessie: One hundred percent me. I outfit plan and very rarely overpack.\n\nNathan: I'm a gypsy. My nickname is Piles, but I somehow always know where everything is.\n\nQ: What untapped destination should people know about?\n\nJessie: I'm very hesitant to share it because it is our paradise, but we love the Dominican Republic. It has some of the most beautiful beaches in the world and is rich with experiences. I love everything about it.\n\nNathan: Mine would be Copenhagen and Denmark, because every time you visit, you can have a totally different experience based on how basic or adventurous you want to be, especially with food.\n\nQ: What is your favorite vacation destination?\n\nJessie: This is difficult, but I have to say Italy. It is just such a beautiful country, and each region holds such magic and is different from the next.\n\nNathan: Dominican Republic. The people, the beaches, the golf and seeing how much joy it brings my kids.\n\nQ: What was a trip you took as a child that stands out?\n\nJessie: Santa Fe. I remember it vividly - the smell of pi\u00f1on wood, going to White Sands, the sound of the bats in the caverns, coyotes howling, eating fry bread from a stand in the middle of the desert. I totally fell for the Southwest forever on that trip. I was five.\n\nNathan: Our family reunion every year in the Tater Hills of Oklahoma where for one weekend a year, mosquito bites were currency.\n\nQ: What's the most important thing you've learned from your travels?\n\nJessie: Have your doctor call in a \"god forbid\" pack of medications.\n\nNathan: Always pack at least two outfits and your basics in your carry-on, and travel in something you could wear to dinner in a pinch.\n\nQ: If you could only pick one place to eat, would you prefer a food truck or fine dining?\n\nJessie: I love a food truck, but I don't love eating standing up or sitting on the curb. I prefer to enjoy a long thoughtful meal, though it doesn't have to necessarily be fancy. I'm going with fine dining.\n\nNathan: Give me a Frito pie and root beer from a truck and I'm one happy camper.\n\nQ: Where are your favorite weekend getaways?\n\nJessie: It would be a tie between Birmingham, Alabama, and Highlands, North Carolina.\n\nNathan: Charleston is 90 minutes door-to-door flight time and my dearest friends Luke and Lauren live there and are always down to show us where the locals like to eat.\n\nQ: What are your five favorite cities?\n\nJessie: Copenhagen, Zurich, London, Barcelona and Rio.\n\nNathan: Milan, Barcelona, Sydney, London and Singapore.\n\nQ: When you go away, what are some of your must-have items?\n\nJessie: Curling iron, journal and travel steamer.\n\nNathan: Golf clubs, peanut M&M's and a Tide pen.\n\nQ: What is your best and/or worst vacation memory?\n\nNathan: Best vacation memory is any summer I get to spend with my family on tour in fun cities. Worst vacation memory is getting sunburned so bad in Australia that my skin came off when I took off my socks.\n\n(Jae-Ha Kim is a New York Times bestselling author and travel writer. You can respond to this column by visiting her website at www.jaehakim.com. Jessie Baylin and Nathan Followill", "body": "Jae-Ha Kim, Tribune Content Agency\n\nFor solo artist Jessie Baylin and Kings of Leon drummer Nathan Followill, this is an especially busy period for the married couple. In May, the Grammy Award-winning Kings of Leon released their latest album \"Can We Please Have Fun.\" And Baylin's May 31 re-release of her critically acclaimed 2018 album \"Strawberry Wind\" - \"Strawberry Wind (Deluxe Edition)\" - also includes new tracks. But with two young children, the musicians are mindful of making sure that one of them is at home with the kids. \"As of right now, I am not going to tour while the Kings are out,\" Baylin said. \"That could change, but I think right now the balance of having one of us home doing the routine with the kids is best.\" Baylin and Followill did this interview from their Nashville home. You may follow them on Instagram (@jezziebaylin and @thenathanfollowill) and X (@doctorfollowill). This interview has been edited for clarity and length.\n\nQ: Do you work on your material at home or on the road or both?\n\nPeople are also reading... Man crashes vintage replica hot rod into Waterloo library moments after purchase East High School student to spend her summer as part of a world-renowned drum and bugle corps Wells gives $1 million to Le Mars daycare center Sioux City sues marina manager for breach of contract UPDATED: Sioux City officers doubted fatal shooting suspect was intoxicated Ceremony marks 175th anniversary of Bruguier's Cabin, Sioux City's oldest structure Sioux City West stuns top-ranked Lewis Central in boys soccer Friday night Nebraska football home game frustrates high school coaches, administators DEAR ABBY: Wealthy in-law 'forgets' promise made to widow Judge dismisses Bertrand defamation against Greenwell, suit continues for school district, ex-employee UPDATED: Leak found in Leif Erikson pool as Riverside aquatic center opens for Memorial Day weekend DEAR ABBY: Relative reveals sordid story to prevent wedding Iowa nurse pays $52,560 to settle million-dollar Medicare fraud case DEAR ABBY: Grieving man's new 'friends' concern wife of four decades Shella Corinne (Parks) Rooney\n\nJessie: All the original material on \"Strawberry Wind\" was written in Nashville over the course of a month - during the strawberry season. The new songs on the deluxe edition were also written while in town this past fall. I think I work best when I'm in the stillness of our home, though.\n\nQ: Jessie, can you share some of your memories of touring with Stevie Nicks?\n\nJessie: Opening for Stevie has been at the top of my mountain of dreams. It has been surreal. The crowds have been kind to me and have really taken in the music and I just love being in her vortex. She truly is one of the most generous of spirit people I have ever known. I love her very much.\n\nQ: When you're not touring, do you prefer to stay at home or take another trip?\n\nNathan: I'm a bit of a homebody. But I also live on a golf course, so I'm happy anywhere that I can get out and chase the little white ball around.\n\nQ: What are some travel memories you'd like to share?\n\nJessie: My parents are wanderlust people, so traveling was a part of my childhood. It wasn't often fancy, but we explored whenever we could. Growing up in New Jersey, the whole eastern coastline was our playground. We would spend time down at the Jersey Shore. Our favorite spot to spend a week every summer was Block Island, Rhode Island. My mom loves the Southwest and her life goal has always been to visit every national park. Right after Nathan and I met, I told him that I was leaving on a three-week family hiking trip through southern Utah. I was very difficult to get in touch with during that time. I think that is when he really fell for me! Nathan and I love exploring the Caribbean together. Our power move is tagging on a bonus holiday at the tail end of a big European tour before heading home.\n\nQ: Where have you traveled to for work that you went back to on a personal trip?\n\nNathan: We played the BottleRock Napa Valley [festival] and unfortunately had to fly in and out, but I always knew that I would go back and explore at some point. My wife and I were fortunate enough to make that happen with an amazing adults-only trip for her birthday.\n\nQ: Nathan, do you recall how you felt watching one of Jessie's shows?\n\nNathan: One of my favorite memories was running 10 blocks across Austin in high-heel boots after my set at SXSW so I could catch her set, and all I could think was, \"I hope I don't stink when I hug her after.\" She was a ball of expression and freedom that seemed like she didn't have a care in the world. I immediately gave her an\"I'm with the drummer\" T-shirt.\n\nQ: Are your children good travelers?\n\nJessie: Violet is a pro, Oliver is less so. [Laughs] He is a pandemic baby, so still a bit feral. But this past year, he's gotten the hang of it.\n\nNathan: As long as there is Wi-Fi, but, yes, they do enjoy it. We are blessed with very curious kids who are adaptive to Mommy and Daddy's lifestyle. Violet has more passport stamps than both my parents combined.\n\nQ: Which of you is the more efficient packer?\n\nJessie: One hundred percent me. I outfit plan and very rarely overpack.\n\nNathan: I'm a gypsy. My nickname is Piles, but I somehow always know where everything is.\n\nQ: What untapped destination should people know about?\n\nJessie: I'm very hesitant to share it because it is our paradise, but we love the Dominican Republic. It has some of the most beautiful beaches in the world and is rich with experiences. I love everything about it.\n\nNathan: Mine would be Copenhagen and Denmark, because every time you visit, you can have a totally different experience based on how basic or adventurous you want to be, especially with food.\n\nQ: What is your favorite vacation destination?\n\nJessie: This is difficult, but I have to say Italy. It is just such a beautiful country, and each region holds such magic and is different from the next.\n\nNathan: Dominican Republic. The people, the beaches, the golf and seeing how much joy it brings my kids.\n\nQ: What was a trip you took as a child that stands out?\n\nJessie: Santa Fe. I remember it vividly - the smell of pi\u00f1on wood, going to White Sands, the sound of the bats in the caverns, coyotes howling, eating fry bread from a stand in the middle of the desert. I totally fell for the Southwest forever on that trip. I was five.\n\nNathan: Our family reunion every year in the Tater Hills of Oklahoma where for one weekend a year, mosquito bites were currency.\n\nQ: What's the most important thing you've learned from your travels?\n\nJessie: Have your doctor call in a \"god forbid\" pack of medications.\n\nNathan: Always pack at least two outfits and your basics in your carry-on, and travel in something you could wear to dinner in a pinch.\n\nQ: If you could only pick one place to eat, would you prefer a food truck or fine dining?\n\nJessie: I love a food truck, but I don't love eating standing up or sitting on the curb. I prefer to enjoy a long thoughtful meal, though it doesn't have to necessarily be fancy. I'm going with fine dining.\n\nNathan: Give me a Frito pie and root beer from a truck and I'm one happy camper.\n\nQ: Where are your favorite weekend getaways?\n\nJessie: It would be a tie between Birmingham, Alabama, and Highlands, North Carolina.\n\nNathan: Charleston is 90 minutes door-to-door flight time and my dearest friends Luke and Lauren live there and are always down to show us where the locals like to eat.\n\nQ: What are your five favorite cities?\n\nJessie: Copenhagen, Zurich, London, Barcelona and Rio.\n\nNathan: Milan, Barcelona, Sydney, London and Singapore.\n\nQ: When you go away, what are some of your must-have items?\n\nJessie: Curling iron, journal and travel steamer.\n\nNathan: Golf clubs, peanut M&M's and a Tide pen.\n\nQ: What is your best and/or worst vacation memory?\n\nNathan: Best vacation memory is any summer I get to spend with my family on tour in fun cities. Worst vacation memory is getting sunburned so bad in Australia that my skin came off when I took off my socks.\n\n(Jae-Ha Kim is a New York Times bestselling author and travel writer. {"uri": "8149144888", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-05-28", "time": "05:11:52", "dateTime": "2024-05-28T05:11:52Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-05-28T05:10:44Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.8784313797950745, "url": "https://napavalleyregister.com/life-entertainment/nation-world/travel/go-away-with-jessie-baylin-and-nathan-followill/article_b12554bd-2600-58f5-b1ea-13fd3871d1e3.html", "title": "Go away with ... Jessie Baylin and Nathan Followill", "body": "Jae-Ha Kim, Tribune Content Agency\n\nFor solo artist Jessie Baylin and Kings of Leon drummer Nathan Followill, this is an especially busy period for the married couple. In May, the Grammy Award-winning Kings of Leon released their latest album \"Can We Please Have Fun.\" And Baylin's May 31 re-release of her critically acclaimed 2018 album \"Strawberry Wind\" - \"Strawberry Wind (Deluxe Edition)\" - also includes new tracks. But with two young children, the musicians are mindful of making sure that one of them is at home with the kids. \"As of right now, I am not going to tour while the Kings are out,\" Baylin said. \"That could change, but I think right now the balance of having one of us home doing the routine with the kids is best.\" Baylin and Followill did this interview from their Nashville home. You may follow them on Instagram (@jezziebaylin and @thenathanfollowill) and X (@doctorfollowill). This interview has been edited for clarity and length.\n\nQ: Do you work on your material at home or on the road or both?\n\nPeople are also reading... Yachts going to BottleRock stuck in Vallejo after bridge failure How much does it cost to rock in Napa? BottleRock fans discuss this year's ticket prices. Woman seriously injured in Napa County crash BottleRock Day 3: Ed Sheeran powers his Napa show through technical glitches Vallejo bridge will remain stuck for about a week, blocking BottleRock boats Horror film explores myths, legends of Napa's Partrick Road BottleRock is coming. Who's starring? And how can you get around Napa? Meet Napa family man, rapper and BottleRock musician Sanho Biagi Bros. president keeps transportation company rolling Grand jury report: Napa County gang activity increasing, including among youth Hours after 2024 Napa BottleRock ends, 2025 tickets go on sale Thousands flock to BottleRock's culinary stage in Napa for Bradley Cooper and Stephen Curry St. Helena police seize concentrated cannabis, vape devices; Calistoga teen arrested Napa's Oxbow RiverStage concert series goes on hiatus as promoters seek new site Napa's BottleRock: eventful on and off the stage\n\nJessie: All the original material on \"Strawberry Wind\" was written in Nashville over the course of a month - during the strawberry season. The new songs on the deluxe edition were also written while in town this past fall. I think I work best when I'm in the stillness of our home, though.\n\nQ: Jessie, can you share some of your memories of touring with Stevie Nicks?\n\nJessie: Opening for Stevie has been at the top of my mountain of dreams. It has been surreal. The crowds have been kind to me and have really taken in the music and I just love being in her vortex. She truly is one of the most generous of spirit people I have ever known. I love her very much.\n\nQ: When you're not touring, do you prefer to stay at home or take another trip?\n\nNathan: I'm a bit of a homebody. But I also live on a golf course, so I'm happy anywhere that I can get out and chase the little white ball around.\n\nQ: What are some travel memories you'd like to share?\n\nJessie: My parents are wanderlust people, so traveling was a part of my childhood. It wasn't often fancy, but we explored whenever we could. Growing up in New Jersey, the whole eastern coastline was our playground. We would spend time down at the Jersey Shore. Our favorite spot to spend a week every summer was Block Island, Rhode Island. My mom loves the Southwest and her life goal has always been to visit every national park. Right after Nathan and I met, I told him that I was leaving on a three-week family hiking trip through southern Utah. I was very difficult to get in touch with during that time. I think that is when he really fell for me! Nathan and I love exploring the Caribbean together. Our power move is tagging on a bonus holiday at the tail end of a big European tour before heading home.\n\nQ: Where have you traveled to for work that you went back to on a personal trip?\n\nNathan: We played the BottleRock Napa Valley [festival] and unfortunately had to fly in and out, but I always knew that I would go back and explore at some point. My wife and I were fortunate enough to make that happen with an amazing adults-only trip for her birthday.\n\nQ: Nathan, do you recall how you felt watching one of Jessie's shows?\n\nNathan: One of my favorite memories was running 10 blocks across Austin in high-heel boots after my set at SXSW so I could catch her set, and all I could think was, \"I hope I don't stink when I hug her after.\" She was a ball of expression and freedom that seemed like she didn't have a care in the world. I immediately gave her an\"I'm with the drummer\" T-shirt.\n\nQ: Are your children good travelers?\n\nJessie: Violet is a pro, Oliver is less so. [Laughs] He is a pandemic baby, so still a bit feral. But this past year, he's gotten the hang of it.\n\nNathan: As long as there is Wi-Fi, but, yes, they do enjoy it. We are blessed with very curious kids who are adaptive to Mommy and Daddy's lifestyle. Violet has more passport stamps than both my parents combined.\n\nQ: Which of you is the more efficient packer?\n\nJessie: One hundred percent me. I outfit plan and very rarely overpack.\n\nNathan: I'm a gypsy. My nickname is Piles, but I somehow always know where everything is.\n\nQ: What untapped destination should people know about?\n\nJessie: I'm very hesitant to share it because it is our paradise, but we love the Dominican Republic. It has some of the most beautiful beaches in the world and is rich with experiences. I love everything about it.\n\nNathan: Mine would be Copenhagen and Denmark, because every time you visit, you can have a totally different experience based on how basic or adventurous you want to be, especially with food.\n\nQ: What is your favorite vacation destination?\n\nJessie: This is difficult, but I have to say Italy. It is just such a beautiful country, and each region holds such magic and is different from the next.\n\nNathan: Dominican Republic. The people, the beaches, the golf and seeing how much joy it brings my kids.\n\nQ: What was a trip you took as a child that stands out?\n\nJessie: Santa Fe. I remember it vividly - the smell of pi\u00f1on wood, going to White Sands, the sound of the bats in the caverns, coyotes howling, eating fry bread from a stand in the middle of the desert. I totally fell for the Southwest forever on that trip. I was five.\n\nNathan: Our family reunion every year in the Tater Hills of Oklahoma where for one weekend a year, mosquito bites were currency.\n\nQ: What's the most important thing you've learned from your travels?\n\nJessie: Have your doctor call in a \"god forbid\" pack of medications.\n\nNathan: Always pack at least two outfits and your basics in your carry-on, and travel in something you could wear to dinner in a pinch.\n\nQ: If you could only pick one place to eat, would you prefer a food truck or fine dining?\n\nJessie: I love a food truck, but I don't love eating standing up or sitting on the curb. I prefer to enjoy a long thoughtful meal, though it doesn't have to necessarily be fancy. I'm going with fine dining.\n\nNathan: Give me a Frito pie and root beer from a truck and I'm one happy camper.\n\nQ: Where are your favorite weekend getaways?\n\nJessie: It would be a tie between Birmingham, Alabama, and Highlands, North Carolina.\n\nNathan: Charleston is 90 minutes door-to-door flight time and my dearest friends Luke and Lauren live there and are always down to show us where the locals like to eat.\n\nQ: What are your five favorite cities?\n\nJessie: Copenhagen, Zurich, London, Barcelona and Rio.\n\nNathan: Milan, Barcelona, Sydney, London and Singapore.\n\nQ: When you go away, what are some of your must-have items?\n\nJessie: Curling iron, journal and travel steamer.\n\nNathan: Golf clubs, peanut M&M's and a Tide pen.\n\nQ: What is your best and/or worst vacation memory?\n\nNathan: Best vacation memory is any summer I get to spend with my family on tour in fun cities. Worst vacation memory is getting sunburned so bad in Australia that my skin came off when I took off my socks.\n\n(Jae-Ha Kim is a New York Times bestselling author and travel writer. You can respond to this column by visiting her website at www.jaehakim.com. You may also follow \"Go Away With...\" on Twitter at @GoAwayWithJae where Jae-Ha Kim welcomes your questions and comments.)\n\nTags Dcc Easytravel101 Wire Tns Travel Kings Of Leon Need to get {"uri": "8149149741", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-05-28", "time": "05:15:51", "dateTime": "2024-05-28T05:15:51Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-05-28T05:14:32Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.8784313797950745, "url": "https://statesville.com/life-entertainment/nation-world/travel/go-away-with-jessie-baylin-and-nathan-followill/article_b6ae095f-447a-516f-96ec-d62a43c1ffa4.html", "title": "Go away with ... Jessie Baylin and Nathan Followill", "body": "Jae-Ha Kim, Tribune Content Agency\n\nFor solo artist Jessie Baylin and Kings of Leon drummer Nathan Followill, this is an especially busy period for the married couple. In May, the Grammy Award-winning Kings of Leon released their latest album \"Can We Please Have Fun.\" And Baylin's May 31 re-release of her critically acclaimed 2018 album \"Strawberry Wind\" - \"Strawberry Wind (Deluxe Edition)\" - also includes new tracks. But with two young children, the musicians are mindful of making sure that one of them is at home with the kids. \"As of right now, I am not going to tour while the Kings are out,\" Baylin said. \"That could change, but I think right now the balance of having one of us home doing the routine with the kids is best.\" Baylin and Followill did this interview from their Nashville home. You may follow them on Instagram (@jezziebaylin and @thenathanfollowill) and X (@doctorfollowill). This interview has been edited for clarity and length.\n\nQ: Do you work on your material at home or on the road or both?\n\nPeople are also reading... Three people found dead in Statesville; baby in the home was not injured North Iredell's Cole Williams recipient of two scholarships Statesville 13-year-old shot, injured; 16-year-old charged with attempted murder Statesville man arrested after road rage incident, standoff Statesville motorcyclist killed in early morning crash on Interstate 77 Statesville High celebrates Class of 2024 Iredell deputies arrest twin brothers on drug charges Statesville Dance and Performing Arts presents 'Around The World' dance recitals Holland Farm Statesville LLC decreases number of homes in planned development Scotts' fifth-grader recognized with Deputy Marty Lewis Citizenship Award Iredell County deputies arrest Florida couple; seize 162 lbs. of marijuana, 4 guns Iredell County Sports Hall of Fame welcomes newest class of inductees North Iredell's Anderson signs with Lenoir-Rhyne Statesville Edward Jones office adds associate financial advisor Grayson Murray dies at age 30 a day after withdrawing from Colonial, PGA Tour says\n\nJessie: All the original material on \"Strawberry Wind\" was written in Nashville over the course of a month - during the strawberry season. The new songs on the deluxe edition were also written while in town this past fall. I think I work best when I'm in the stillness of our home, though.\n\nQ: Jessie, can you share some of your memories of touring with Stevie Nicks?\n\nJessie: Opening for Stevie has been at the top of my mountain of dreams. It has been surreal. The crowds have been kind to me and have really taken in the music and I just love being in her vortex. She truly is one of the most generous of spirit people I have ever known. I love her very much.\n\nQ: When you're not touring, do you prefer to stay at home or take another trip?\n\nNathan: I'm a bit of a homebody. But I also live on a golf course, so I'm happy anywhere that I can get out and chase the little white ball around.\n\nQ: What are some travel memories you'd like to share?\n\nJessie: My parents are wanderlust people, so traveling was a part of my childhood. It wasn't often fancy, but we explored whenever we could. Growing up in New Jersey, the whole eastern coastline was our playground. We would spend time down at the Jersey Shore. Our favorite spot to spend a week every summer was Block Island, Rhode Island. My mom loves the Southwest and her life goal has always been to visit every national park. Right after Nathan and I met, I told him that I was leaving on a three-week family hiking trip through southern Utah. I was very difficult to get in touch with during that time. I think that is when he really fell for me! Nathan and I love exploring the Caribbean together. Our power move is tagging on a bonus holiday at the tail end of a big European tour before heading home.\n\nQ: Where have you traveled to for work that you went back to on a personal trip?\n\nNathan: We played the BottleRock Napa Valley [festival] and unfortunately had to fly in and out, but I always knew that I would go back and explore at some point. My wife and I were fortunate enough to make that happen with an amazing adults-only trip for her birthday.\n\nQ: Nathan, do you recall how you felt watching one of Jessie's shows?\n\nNathan: One of my favorite memories was running 10 blocks across Austin in high-heel boots after my set at SXSW so I could catch her set, and all I could think was, \"I hope I don't stink when I hug her after.\" She was a ball of expression and freedom that seemed like she didn't have a care in the world. I immediately gave her an\"I'm with the drummer\" T-shirt.\n\nQ: Are your children good travelers?\n\nJessie: Violet is a pro, Oliver is less so. [Laughs] He is a pandemic baby, so still a bit feral. But this past year, he's gotten the hang of it.\n\nNathan: As long as there is Wi-Fi, but, yes, they do enjoy it. We are blessed with very curious kids who are adaptive to Mommy and Daddy's lifestyle. Violet has more passport stamps than both my parents combined.\n\nQ: Which of you is the more efficient packer?\n\nJessie: One hundred percent me. I outfit plan and very rarely overpack.\n\nNathan: I'm a gypsy. My nickname is Piles, but I somehow always know where everything is.\n\nQ: What untapped destination should people know about?\n\nJessie: I'm very hesitant to share it because it is our paradise, but we love the Dominican Republic. It has some of the most beautiful beaches in the world and is rich with experiences. I love everything about it.\n\nNathan: Mine would be Copenhagen and Denmark, because every time you visit, you can have a totally different experience based on how basic or adventurous you want to be, especially with food.\n\nQ: What is your favorite vacation destination?\n\nJessie: This is difficult, but I have to say Italy. It is just such a beautiful country, and each region holds such magic and is different from the next.\n\nNathan: Dominican Republic. The people, the beaches, the golf and seeing how much joy it brings my kids.\n\nQ: What was a trip you took as a child that stands out?\n\nJessie: Santa Fe. I remember it vividly - the smell of pi\u00f1on wood, going to White Sands, the sound of the bats in the caverns, coyotes howling, eating fry bread from a stand in the middle of the desert. I totally fell for the Southwest forever on that trip. I was five.\n\nNathan: Our family reunion every year in the Tater Hills of Oklahoma where for one weekend a year, mosquito bites were currency.\n\nQ: What's the most important thing you've learned from your travels?\n\nJessie: Have your doctor call in a \"god forbid\" pack of medications.\n\nNathan: Always pack at least two outfits and your basics in your carry-on, and travel in something you could wear to dinner in a pinch.\n\nQ: If you could only pick one place to eat, would you prefer a food truck or fine dining?\n\nJessie: I love a food truck, but I don't love eating standing up or sitting on the curb. I prefer to enjoy a long thoughtful meal, though it doesn't have to necessarily be fancy. I'm going with fine dining.\n\nNathan: Give me a Frito pie and root beer from a truck and I'm one happy camper.\n\nQ: Where are your favorite weekend getaways?\n\nJessie: It would be a tie between Birmingham, Alabama, and Highlands, North Carolina.\n\nNathan: Charleston is 90 minutes door-to-door flight time and my dearest friends Luke and Lauren live there and are always down to show us where the locals like to eat.\n\nQ: What are your five favorite cities?\n\nJessie: Copenhagen, Zurich, London, Barcelona and Rio.\n\nNathan: Milan, Barcelona, Sydney, London and Singapore.\n\nQ: When you go away, what are some of your must-have items?\n\nJessie: Curling iron, journal and travel steamer.\n\nNathan: Golf clubs, peanut M&M's and a Tide pen.\n\nQ: What is your best and/or worst vacation memory?\n\nNathan: Best vacation memory is any summer I get to spend with my family on tour in fun cities. Worst vacation memory is getting sunburned so bad in Australia that my skin came off when I took off my socks.\n\n(Jae-Ha Kim is a New York Times bestselling author and travel writer. You can respond to this column by visiting her website at www.jaehakim.com. You may also follow \"Go Away With...\" on Twitter at @GoAwayWithJae where Jae-Ha Kim welcomes your questions and comments.)\n\nTags Dcc Easytravel101 Wire Tns Travel Kings Of Leon Need to get Violet has more passport stamps than both my parents combined.\n\nQ: Which of you is the more efficient packer?\n\nJessie: One hundred percent me. My nickname is Piles, but I somehow always know where everything is.\n\nQ: What untapped destination should people know about?\n\nJessie: I'm very hesitant to share it because it is our paradise, but we love the Dominican Republic. I was five.\n\nNathan: Our family reunion every year in the Tater Hills of Oklahoma where for one weekend a year, mosquito bites were currency.\n\nQ: What's the most important thing you've learned from your travels?\n\nJessie: Have your doctor call in a \"god forbid\" pack of medications.\n\nNathan: Always pack at least two outfits and your basics in your carry-on, and travel in something you could wear to dinner in a pinch.\n\nQ: If you could only pick one place to eat, would you prefer a food truck or fine dining?\n\nJessie: I love a food truck, but I don't love eating standing up or sitting on the curb. I prefer to enjoy a long thoughtful meal, though it doesn't have to necessarily be fancy. I'm going with fine dining.\n\nNathan: Give me a Frito pie and root beer from a truck and I'm one happy camper.\n\nQ: Where are your favorite weekend getaways?\n\nJessie: It would be a tie between Birmingham, Alabama, and Highlands, North Carolina.\n\nNathan: Charleston is 90 minutes door-to-door flight time and my dearest friends Luke and Lauren live there and are always down to show us where the locals like to eat.\n\nQ: What are your five favorite cities?\n\nJessie: Copenhagen, Zurich, London, Barcelona and Rio.\n\nNathan: Milan, Barcelona, Sydney, London and Singapore.\n\nQ: When you go away, what are some of your must-have items?\n\nJessie: Curling iron, journal and travel steamer.\n\nNathan: Golf clubs, peanut M&M's and a Tide pen.\n\nQ: What is your best and/or worst vacation memory?\n\nNathan: Best vacation memory is any summer I get to spend with my family on tour in fun cities. Worst vacation memory is getting sunburned so bad in Australia that my skin came off when I took off my socks.\n\n(Jae-Ha Kim is a New York Times bestselling author and travel writer. I think I work best when I'm in the stillness of our home, though.\n\nQ: Jessie, can you share some of your memories of touring with Stevie Nicks?\n\nJessie: Opening for Stevie has been at the top of my mountain of dreams. It has been surreal. The crowds have been kind to me and have really taken in the music and I just love being in her vortex. She truly is one of the most generous of spirit people I have ever known. I love her very much.\n\nQ: When you're not touring, do you prefer to stay at home or take another trip?\n\nNathan: I'm a bit of a homebody. But I also live on a golf course, so I'm happy anywhere that I can get out and chase the little white ball around.\n\nQ: What are some travel memories you'd like to share?\n\nJessie: My parents are wanderlust people, so traveling was a part of my childhood. It wasn't often fancy, but we explored whenever we could. Growing up in New Jersey, the whole eastern coastline was our playground. We would spend time down at the Jersey Shore. Our favorite spot to spend a week every summer was Block Island, Rhode Island. My mom loves the Southwest and her life goal has always been to visit every national park. Right after Nathan and I met, I told him that I was leaving on a three-week family hiking trip through southern Utah. I was very difficult to get in touch with during that time. I think that is when he really fell for me! Nathan and I love exploring the Caribbean together. Our power move is tagging on a bonus holiday at the tail end of a big European tour before heading home.\n\nQ: Where have you traveled to for work that you went back to on a personal trip?\n\nNathan: We played the BottleRock Napa Valley [festival] and unfortunately had to fly in and out, but I always knew that I would go back and explore at some point. My wife and I were fortunate enough to make that happen with an amazing adults-only trip for her birthday.\n\nQ: Nathan, do you recall how you felt watching one of Jessie's shows?\n\nNathan: One of my favorite memories was running 10 blocks across Austin in high-heel boots after my set at SXSW so I could catch her set, and all I could think was, \"I hope I don't stink when I hug her after.\" She was a ball of expression and freedom that seemed like she didn't have a care in the world. I immediately gave her an\"I'm with the drummer\" T-shirt.\n\nQ: Are your children good travelers?\n\nJessie: Violet is a pro, Oliver is less so. [Laughs] He is a pandemic baby, so still a bit feral. But this past year, he's gotten the hang of it.\n\nNathan: As long as there is Wi-Fi, but, yes, they do enjoy it. We are blessed with very curious kids who are adaptive to Mommy and Daddy's lifestyle. Violet has more passport stamps than both my parents combined.\n\nQ: Which of you is the more efficient packer?\n\nJessie: One hundred percent me. I outfit plan and very rarely overpack.\n\nNathan: I'm a gypsy. My nickname is Piles, but I somehow always know where everything is.\n\nQ: What untapped destination should people know about?\n\nJessie: I'm very hesitant to share it because it is our paradise, but we love the Dominican Republic. It has some of the most beautiful beaches in the world and is rich with experiences. I love everything about it.\n\nNathan: Mine would be Copenhagen and Denmark, because every time you visit, you can have a totally different experience based on how basic or adventurous you want to be, especially with food.\n\nQ: What is your favorite vacation destination?\n\nJessie: This is difficult, but I have to say Italy. It is just such a beautiful country, and each region holds such magic and is different from the next.\n\nNathan: Dominican Republic. The people, the beaches, the golf and seeing how much joy it brings my kids.\n\nQ: What was a trip you took as a child that stands out?\n\nJessie: Santa Fe. I remember it vividly - the smell of pi\u00f1on wood, going to White Sands, the sound of the bats in the caverns, coyotes howling, eating fry bread from a stand in the middle of the desert. I totally fell for the Southwest forever on that trip. I was five.\n\nNathan: Our family reunion every year in the Tater Hills of Oklahoma where for one weekend a year, mosquito bites were currency.\n\nQ: What's the most important thing you've learned from your travels?\n\nJessie: Have your doctor call in a \"god forbid\" pack of medications.\n\nNathan: Always pack at least two outfits and your basics in your carry-on, and travel in something you could wear to dinner in a pinch.\n\nQ: If you could only pick one place to eat, would you prefer a food truck or fine dining?\n\nJessie: I love a food truck, but I don't love eating standing up or sitting on the curb. I prefer to enjoy a long thoughtful meal, though it doesn't have to necessarily be fancy. I'm going with fine dining.\n\nNathan: Give me a Frito pie and root beer from a truck and I'm one happy camper.\n\nQ: Where are your favorite weekend getaways?\n\nJessie: It would be a tie between Birmingham, Alabama, and Highlands, North Carolina.\n\nNathan: Charleston is 90 minutes door-to-door flight time and my dearest friends Luke and Lauren live there and are always down to show us where the locals like to eat.\n\nQ: What are your five favorite cities?\n\nJessie: Copenhagen, Zurich, London, Barcelona and Rio.\n\nNathan: Milan, Barcelona, Sydney, London and Singapore.\n\nQ: When you go away, what are some of your must-have items?\n\nJessie: Curling iron, journal and travel steamer.\n\nNathan: Golf clubs, peanut M&M's and a Tide pen.\n\nQ: What is your best and/or worst vacation memory?\n\nNathan: Best vacation memory is any summer I get to spend with my family on tour in fun cities. Worst vacation memory is getting sunburned so bad in Australia that my skin came off when I took off my socks.\n\n(Jae-Ha Kim is a New York Times bestselling author and travel writer.
